Yes, secondary dimensions are present and do not compete with the primary classification but extend it. *Cognitive dimension (secondary):* Phili2:3 — humility as counting others more significant is a cognitive reordering; Pro11:2 — humility opens the person to wisdom, engaging the cognitive faculty. *Affective dimension (secondary):* 2Ki22:19 and 2Ch34:27 pair humbling with weeping; 2Cor12:21 names the grief produced by God's humbling; the characteristic has an affective correlate even when it is not primarily an emotion. *Condition/state dimension (secondary):* M09-B evidences that lowliness is not only the volitional act (M09-A) but also the state in which the person may find themselves — the condition register. The secondary dimensions do not compete with the volitional-dispositional primary; rather, they show the characteristic engaging multiple faculties in its operation, with the will as the primary constitutional location and affect and cognition as its operational partners.

  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T2.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

None of these compete with the volitional-primary classification; they evidence the characteristic engaging multiple faculties with the will as constitutional anchor.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

*Re-reading §3.E fresh for T2's lens.*

---

### T2

#### T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

##### T2.1.1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The M09-B corpus provides the clearest spirit-level locating: Psa107:12 (outside the primary evidence but referenced in the carry-forward; within-corpus note: the ka.na imposed instances in M09-B evidence the spirit-level by God bowing "hearts down" — the innermost faculty). Within the primary evidence, the spirit-level location is implicit rather than explicit in most verses. However, the overall constitutional depth implied by the characteristic is consistent with spirit-level operation: Lev26:41 names the "uncircumcised heart" as the site of the humbling; 2Ch34:27 pairs humbling with a "tender heart" — constitutional language that in the programme framework operates at the heart level bordering on spirit.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The Submission corpus does not explicitly name the spirit level as the location of the characteristic. The heart (Rom6:17; Eph6:5; Col3:22) and conscience (Phili2:12) are the named constitutional locations. The spirit level is not directly named in §3.A.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, explicitly in both verses. Psa34:18 — "the crushed in spirit" (dak.ka-ruach) — ruach is the Hebrew word for spirit; the spirit is the explicit constitutional location. Isa57:15 — "with him who is of a contrite and lowly spirit" (dak.ka-ve-shpal-ruach) and "to revive the spirit of the lowly" — the spirit is named twice, establishing it as the primary constitutional site of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not explicitly name the spirit level as the location of meekness or gentleness. Heb5:2 names the capacity as an inner quality of the high priest without specifying the constitutional level. Act9:38 names the quality of volitional responsiveness without specifying the spirit level.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not explicitly name the spirit level as the constitutional location of semnotēs. The characteristic is named as an inner quality without specifying the spirit as its constitutional site.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes, explicitly in Psa51:12 — "uphold me with a willing spirit" (ruach nedivah — a willing/free-spirited spirit). Ruach (spirit) is the explicit constitutional location in this verse. The willing spirit is the spirit characterised by free, uncoerced inner readiness for God — the spirit-level being the deepest constitutional location named for the characteristic in this corpus.

---

##### T2.1.2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence does not explicitly identify humility's origin as spirit-level, but it points in that direction. The heart-location (Mat11:29 — "lowly in heart"; Lev26:41 — uncircumcised heart) suggests the characteristic operates at the deepest personal level. The contrast between performed humility (Col2:23 — "no value in stopping the indulgence of the flesh") and genuine inner transformation implies that genuine humility operates at a level deeper than conscious self-management — the level at which genuine character-transformation occurs. The constitutional depth required for the characteristic is consistent with spirit-level origin, even where the language does not explicitly name it.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Not directly, but the depth implied by several verses is consistent with spirit-level operation. 1Pe1:22 — obedience to truth "purifies the soul itself" — a depth of inner operation that suggests transformation at a level below ordinary volition. Heb5:8 — Christ "learning" obedience through suffering implies a deep interior process of formation rather than surface-level compliance. The "sincere heart" language (Eph6:5; Col3:22) and "fear of God" (Phili2:12; Col3:22) suggest the characteristic's genuine form operates at the deepest personal level, consistent with spirit-level origin, though not explicitly named as such.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes. The primary vocabulary in both verses is ruach (spirit) — the spirit is the constitutional level most directly named as the location of the crushed/contrite state. The heart is also named (Psa34:18 — brokenhearted; Isa57:15 — "revive the heart of the contrite") but the spirit is the first-named and dominant location. The origin-point of the characteristic is the spirit-level — the crushing reaches the spirit first; the heart is the secondary constitutional level named in relation to it.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence does not directly evidence spirit-level origin. The grounding of metriopatheō in "shared weakness" (Heb5:2) suggests the characteristic originates in a self-knowledge that may reach the spirit level, but this is inferred beyond the text.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence does not directly evidence spirit-level origin. The settled inner gravity implied by semnotēs may operate at the spirit level, but this is inferred beyond the text.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Psa51:12 evidences the spirit as the constitutional level at which willing-heartedness resides and from which it must be divinely restored after failure. The spirit is the origin point in the VCG-02 register — God upholds the spirit and the spirit's willing quality is thereby restored. In VCG-01, the heart is the primary constitutional location (Exo35:5/22; 2Ch29:31 — "willing heart"). Whether the spirit or heart is primary origin is register-dependent: in VCG-01, the heart; in VCG-02, the spirit.

---

##### T2.1.3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

To the extent spirit-level location is implied, it reveals that humility is not achievable by surface-level adjustment or external discipline alone. The Colossian exposure of false humility (Col2:18; Col2:23) evidences that self-imposed severity — operating at the level of conscious behaviour and physical practice — cannot produce genuine humility, which requires a transformation at a level below conscious management. This is consistent with spirit-level depth: the genuine characteristic must be generated from the innermost person, not merely adopted at the behavioural surface. The heart-language of Lev26:41 ("uncircumcised heart") and Mat11:29 ("lowly in heart") confirms that the genuine article operates at constitutional depth.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

To the extent spirit-level depth is implied (T2.1.2), it reveals that genuine submission cannot be produced by surface-level pressure or social accountability alone. Phili2:12 — the sustained obedience that must persist "much more in my absence" (when external accountability is removed) requires an origin deeper than socially-accountable compliance — the conscience and fear of God replace the apostle. This implies an inner-generativity of the characteristic that is consistent with spirit-level depth: the person who genuinely submits does so from an inner posture that does not require external support, suggesting the characteristic is generated at a constitutional depth below the social-relational surface.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Spirit-level location reveals that contrition is the deepest possible inner-being state — it reaches the innermost constitutional level of the person. A breaking that is only at the surface (emotion, behaviour) without reaching the spirit would not be genuine contrition in the biblical sense. Isa57:15's framing — the high-and-holy God dwelling with the contrite spirit — implies that the spirit-level location makes the characteristic the point of closest divine-human contact: where the person's spirit is genuinely crushed, God's spirit revives. The constitutional depth of the characteristic (spirit-level) is what makes it the site of the deepest divine-human encounter.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

Spirit-level location is not directly evidenced in the two-verse corpus. The depth implied by genuine metriopatheō (grounded in shared creaturely vulnerability, not in surface performance) is consistent with spirit-level operation, but the evidence does not name this explicitly.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

Spirit-level location is not directly evidenced. The characteristic's depth as a settled character quality is consistent with spirit-level operation but is not named as such in §3.D.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Psa51:12's spirit-level location reveals that willing-heartedness operates at the deepest constitutional level of the person — the spirit as the innermost faculty. When the spirit is burdened by moral failure (Psa51 context), the willing quality of the spirit is lost and cannot be self-restored; it requires divine upholding. This depth of constitutional location explains why willing-heartedness cannot be coerced: external compulsion cannot reach the spirit level to produce genuine willingness — it can only produce outer compliance while the spirit remains unwilling or burdened.

---

##### T2.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent but is primarily indirect on this point (see T2.1.1–T2.1.3). The characteristic is consistently located in the heart and at constitutional depth; the spirit level is implied by the depth of the language rather than named explicitly. The most explicit spirit-language would come from the contrition register (dak.ka in CHAR-3, which names "crushed in spirit") rather than this characteristic's primary vocabulary.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not fully silent but is primarily indirect regarding spirit-level location (see T2.1.1–T2.1.3). The primary explicit constitutional location is the heart and conscience; spirit-level depth is implied by the depth of transformation evidenced.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent; spirit-level location is explicit and primary (see T2.1.1–T2.1.3).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit spirit-level location. Constitutional depth is implied but not named at the spirit level in §3.C.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit spirit-level location for semnotēs.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence is not silent; spirit-level location is explicitly evidenced in Psa51:12 (see T2.1.1–T2.1.3).

---

#### T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

##### T2.2.1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Mat11:29 provides the most relevant soul-level connexion: "you will find rest for your souls" — the result of learning humility and gentleness from Christ. The *soul* is named as the beneficiary of the rest that Christ's lowly-in-heart character produces. This does not locate humility itself at the soul level but identifies the soul as the constitutional level that receives the characteristic's fruit. The connexion is indirect: humility produces rest; that rest is received at the soul level. Within the Phili2:8 context, Christ's self-humbling produces the obedience that is the act of the will, and the M09-B register (experienced lowliness) names states that affect the person holistically, including at the soul level.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, explicitly. 1Pe1:22 — "having purified your souls by your obedience to the truth" — the soul is the constitutional level that obedience to truth acts upon and purifies. The soul's purification is the direct product of sustained obedience; this places the soul as the constitutional level that submission both engages and transforms. The phrasing "purified your souls" indicates that the characteristic's operation reaches the soul's deepest faculty.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The heart (lev/lebab in Hebrew) is explicitly named: Psa34:18 — "brokenhearted" (nishbar-lev). In Hebrew anthropology, lev (heart) encompasses what the programme framework would treat as soul-level functions (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness). The heart as constitutional location confirms soul-level operation alongside the spirit-level. Isa57:15 — "revive the heart of the contrite" — the heart's reviving as the outcome of God's dwelling with the contrite evidences the soul-level engagement.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not explicitly name the soul level as the constitutional location of meekness or gentleness. The terms name capacities and qualities of engagement without specifying the soul as their location.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not explicitly name the soul level as the constitutional location of semnotēs. The characteristic is named as an inner quality shaping the person's manner of existence without specifying the soul as its site.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The heart (lev) is explicitly named as a constitutional location: Exo35:5 — "generous/willing heart"; Exo35:22 — "willing heart"; 2Ch29:31 — "willing heart." In Hebrew anthropology, lev (heart) encompasses the soul's integrating functions (knowing, willing, feeling). The heart as constitutional location confirms soul-level engagement — the character is located in the soul's integrating centre.

---

##### T2.2.2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The soul-level connexion via Mat11:29 reveals that humility, while constitutionally located primarily in the heart and will, produces its fruit at the level of the deepest personal experience — the soul finding rest. This suggests the characteristic has a reach that extends beyond its constitutional origin: it is generated in the will/heart, but its effect penetrates to the level of the person's most foundational experience of themselves before God. The rest the soul finds is not merely circumstantial calm but the settlement that comes from no longer needing to assert, protect, or elevate the self — the soul ceases striving when the will has genuinely released the claim to standing.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

1Pe1:22 reveals that submission, as obedience to truth, is not merely an outer behavioural disposition but one that reaches and transforms the innermost personal level. The soul's purification suggests the characteristic operates as a sanctifying force within the person's deepest self — not only orienting behaviour but reshaping the person at the level of their most foundational inner experience. The fruit produced (sincere brotherly love from a pure heart) is not a merely rational conclusion but an affective-characterological product of this deep inner transformation, confirming that the soul-level operation is genuine and not merely metaphorical.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Psa34:18's "brokenhearted" reveals that contrition operates at the soul's integrating centre — the heart as the seat of knowing, willing, feeling, and moral awareness is broken. This depth of soul-level operation confirms that contrition is not a surface emotional state but a condition that reaches the inner person's integrating faculty. Isa57:15's "revive the heart of the contrite" confirms that the soul-level operation requires divine reviving — the characteristic at soul-level depth cannot restore itself but requires God's reviving action.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

Soul-level location is not explicitly evidenced in §3.C. The characteristic's operation at the inner-person level is implied by its nature as an inner quality, but the soul is not named.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

Soul-level location is not explicitly evidenced in §3.D.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The heart-location (Exo35:5/22; 2Ch29:31) reveals that willing-heartedness operates at the soul's integrating centre — not in a single faculty (will alone, or affect alone) but in the heart that integrates knowing, willing, and feeling together. The willing heart is one whose integrating centre is freely-moved toward God — the whole person's inner integration is oriented toward free giving rather than reluctant compliance. The soul-level location confirms that the characteristic is a whole-person orientation rather than a single-faculty operation.

---

##### T2.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent but is primarily indirect (see T2.2.1 and T2.2.2). The soul level appears as the recipient of the characteristic's fruit (rest) rather than as its primary constitutional location.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; soul-level location is explicitly evidenced in 1Pe1:22 (see T2.2.1 and T2.2.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent; soul-level location is explicitly evidenced through the heart-location in both verses (see T2.2.1 and T2.2.2).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit soul-level location.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit soul-level location.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence is not silent; soul-level location is explicitly evidenced through the heart-location in VCG-01 (see T2.2.1 and T2.2.2).

---

#### T2.3 — Heart

##### T2.3.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, the heart-location is explicit and primary. Mat11:29 — "I am gentle and lowly in heart" — is the definitive verse: lowliness (tapeinos) is located explicitly in the heart (kardia) as a self-description of Jesus. Lev26:41 — "their uncircumcised heart is humbled" — the humbling is located in the heart, which must be broken from its hardness. 2Ki22:19 — "your heart was penitent, and you humbled yourself" — the penitent heart is paired with the humbling as its constitutional location. 2Ch34:27 — "your heart was tender and you humbled yourself" — the tender heart and the humbling are inseparably paired. Across the corpus, the heart is the site from which the characteristic originates and in which it is genuinely present or absent.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, explicitly and primarily. Rom6:17 — "obedient from the heart to the standard of teaching" — heart-location is explicit and is used to distinguish genuine from merely external obedience. Eph6:5 — "with a sincere heart" — the heart's genuineness is the criterion of authentic submission. Col3:22 — "sincerity of heart" versus "eye-service" — the heart is the site where submission's authenticity is determined. Luk17:10 — the servant's inner self-assessment ("we are unworthy servants") — the posture of submission is a heart-level self-assessment. The heart is the constitutionally definitive location for the genuine form of this characteristic across the M09-C corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Psa34:18 — "brokenhearted" (nishbar-lev — the heart/lev broken/shattered). Isa57:15 — "revive the heart of the contrite" — the heart is the constitutional level that receives God's reviving response to the contrite state. Heart-location is explicit in both verses, confirming it as a primary constitutional site alongside the spirit.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not explicitly locate meekness or gentleness in the heart. Heb5:2 names the capacity for gentle dealing without heart-location; Act9:38 names volitional responsiveness without heart-location. Heart-location must be inferred from the nature of the characteristic rather than directly evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not explicitly locate semnotēs in the heart. The characteristic is named as an inner quality without heart-location specification.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes, explicitly and as the primary constitutional location in VCG-01. Exo35:5 — "generous/willing heart" (lev nadav); Exo35:22 — "willing heart" (lev nadiv); 2Ch29:31 — "willing heart" (lev nadiv). All three VCG-01 verses name the heart (lev) as the constitutional location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional site across the five-verse corpus (3 of 5 verses name it explicitly).

---

##### T2.3.2 — What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The heart in biblical usage integrates knowing, willing, feeling, and moral awareness — all of which are engaged by humility. The Lev26:41 "uncircumcised heart" language suggests the heart's moral-knowing function: the hardened heart is one that does not genuinely receive or register the moral reality of its situation before God. The 2Ki22:19 "penitent heart" engages the heart's affective and moral-awareness dimensions — genuine inner grief over one's condition. Mat11:29 "lowly in heart" engages the heart's dispositional-volitional function — the settled posture of the whole person. Phili2:3 ("in humility count others more significant") engages the heart's cognitive-evaluative function — the reassessment of relative worth. The characteristic engages the heart's integrating function comprehensively: knowing (accurate self-assessment), willing (the act of self-lowering), feeling (the grief and tenderness that accompany genuine humbling), and moral awareness (recognition of one's true standing before God).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The heart-location engages the heart's *integrating moral and volitional function*. Rom6:17 — "obedience from the heart" contrasts with enslaved-to-sin; the heart's integrating moral orientation (whose authority rules the person) is what is at stake. Eph6:5 — "sincere heart" engages the heart's authenticity-function — the undivided inner person whose will and motive are aligned. Col3:22 — "sincerity of heart and fear of the Lord" engages the heart's moral-reverential orientation. The characteristic engages the heart as the integrating centre that determines: (a) whose authority the person genuinely serves (volitional-allegiance function); (b) whether compliance is whole-hearted or divided (sincerity function); (c) what moves the person at their deepest level (motivational function).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The heart's breaking (Psa34:18) reveals that contrition engages the heart's *integrating function comprehensively*: the heart as the centre of knowing, willing, feeling, and moral awareness is broken — not one function only but the integrating centre itself. When the heart is broken, the integrating function that holds the person together before God is genuinely disrupted. Isa57:15's "revive the heart" indicates that the restoration God provides is equally comprehensive — reaching the heart's integrating function to restore it. The heart-location confirms that contrition is a whole-person inner event, not a compartmentalised emotional state.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

Heart-location is not explicitly evidenced in §3.C. The characteristic's grounding in shared weakness (Heb5:2) implies a heart-level self-awareness, but the heart is not named as the constitutional site.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

Heart-location is not explicitly evidenced in §3.D.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The heart's location reveals that willing-heartedness engages the heart's *integrating volitional-affective function*. The "generous/willing heart" (Exo35:5) is one whose integrating centre is freely-moved toward giving — the heart's knowing, willing, and feeling are all aligned in the direction of free offering rather than in conflict (reluctance would be the heart's conflicted state). The characteristic in its heart-location is the whole-person inner integration that produces the uncoerced external act of giving.

---

##### T2.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is explicit and primary (see T2.3.1 and T2.3.2).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is explicit and primary (see T2.3.1 and T2.3.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is explicit in both verses (see T2.3.1 and T2.3.2).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location. The secondary anchor Mat11:29 ("gentle and lowly in heart") would establish heart-location but is not in §3.C and cannot be cited as evidence for this batch.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit heart-location for semnotēs. The characteristic's inner quality is named without naming the heart as its constitutional site.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is explicit and primary in VCG-01 (see T2.3.1 and T2.3.2).

---

#### T2.4 — Mind

##### T2.4.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The mind is engaged indirectly. Phili2:3 — "in humility count others more significant than yourselves" — requires a cognitive act of evaluation and re-ordering that engages the mind's assessing function, even though the word "mind" (nous) is not named. Col2:18 names the "sensuous mind" (nous tēs sarkos) as the faculty that is puffed up in false humility, making the mind the site of the distortion of the characteristic. The contrast in Col2:23 (appearance of wisdom — humility's cognitive dimension exposed as appearance) further engages the mind. The characteristic thus involves the mind as the seat of evaluation and cognitive reordering, though the primary location remains the heart and will.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, directly in 2Cor10:5 — "take every thought captive to obey Christ." The mind is the site of engagement: the "arguments and every lofty opinion raised against the knowledge of God" are cognitive contents; taking "every thought" (noēma — thought, reasoning) captive is a cognitive-volitional act that positions the mind's operations under Christ's authority. The mind is not merely the instrument of submission but the battleground where the characteristic is won or lost — proud reasoning is the specific resistance that submission must overcome.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not explicitly name the mind as a constitutional location for contrition. The spirit and heart are the named constitutional locations. While genuine contrition involves accurate cognitive self-assessment (knowing one has failed), the mind as a distinct faculty is not named in this corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not explicitly locate meekness or gentleness in the mind. The cognitive self-assessment of shared weakness (Heb5:2) engages the cognitive faculty but does not name the mind as a constitutional location.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not explicitly locate semnotēs in the mind. The characteristic is a quality of character and manner rather than a named mind-located phenomenon.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The five-verse corpus does not explicitly locate willing-heartedness in the mind. The named constitutional locations are heart (VCG-01) and spirit (VCG-02). The mind as a distinct constitutional faculty is not named in §3.E.

---

##### T2.4.2 — What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The Phili2:3 evidence reveals that humility engages the mind's evaluative function: the cognitive act of *counting* (hēgeomai — reckoning, considering, evaluating) others as more significant is a deliberate cognitive operation. The Col2:18 evidence reveals that the mind can be the site of false humility's corruption: the "sensuous mind" inflated while performing humility. Together these evidences reveal that humility engages the mind's capacity for honest self-assessment and other-evaluation — the function of realistic comparative judgment. The mind's role is to arrive at an accurate rather than self-inflated assessment of relative worth; humility is the disposition that enables this accurate assessment.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

2Cor10:5 reveals that submission engages the mind's *evaluative and reasoning function*. The "arguments and lofty opinions raised against the knowledge of God" are intellectual-evaluative constructs — the mind's capacity to generate self-justifying reasoning that resists divine authority. Submission requires capturing this evaluative capacity and reorienting it under Christ's authority. The mind's function in this characteristic is not merely to understand the command but to surrender its own reasoning to the authority's claim — which is a higher-level cognitive act. 2Cor10:6 ("when your obedience is complete") positions the community's collective cognitive-volitional state as the determining factor.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location (see T2.4.1). The cognitive dimension is implied by the characteristic's requirement for genuine moral self-knowledge, but the mind is not named as a constitutional site in this corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

Mind-location is not explicitly evidenced in §3.C. The enabling cognitive self-assessment (awareness of shared weakness) is implied but not located in the mind as a named constitutional site.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

Mind-location is not evidenced in §3.D.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

Mind-location is not evidenced in §3.E.

---

##### T2.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; mind-engagement is present but indirect (see T2.4.1 and T2.4.2). The heart remains the primary location; the mind is a secondary site of engagement.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; mind-location is explicitly evidenced in 2Cor10:5 (see T2.4.1 and T2.4.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location. The characteristic's primary constitutional locations are spirit and heart (see T2.1.1 and T2.3.1). Mind-engagement is implied but not named.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on mind-location for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location for willing-heartedness. The primary locations are heart and spirit.

---

#### T2.5 — Other Soul Subsets

##### T2.5.1 — Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence surfaces the will as a distinct soul-level location beyond heart and mind. The characteristic is repeatedly framed as an act of the will: "humble yourselves" (Jam4:10; 1Pe5:6) — reflexive imperatives addressed to the volitional capacity; Phili2:8 — Christ "humbled himself" — the volitional self-determination of the kenotic act. The will's engagement with humility is as a primary faculty, not merely as the instrument of the heart's orientation. Additionally, the affect — weeping, tenderness, grief (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27; 2Cor12:21) — surfaces as a soul-level location in which the characteristic finds its expression.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The conscience is surfaced as a distinct soul-level location. Phili2:12 — sustained obedience rooted in "fear of God rather than social pressure" — the conscience functions as the internal accountability when external accountability is absent. Eph6:1 — "in the Lord, for this is right" — the moral-rightness evaluation that grounds the obedience is a conscience-function. Col3:22 — "fearing the Lord" as the inner motivational ground — fear of God as a conscience-orientation. The conscience is the inner faculty that evaluates the legitimacy of the authority claim and sustains the submission when external supports are withdrawn.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

Beyond the heart (explicitly named) and the spirit (explicitly named), the two-verse corpus does not surface additional soul-level locations. The corpus is focused on spirit and heart as the primary constitutional locations.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The will is surfaced as the primary constitutional location by the evidence (T1.8.1): both metriopatheō and okneō evidence volitional qualities — the will's manner of engaging (measured, calibrated) and the will's kinetic quality (without hesitation). The will is the most directly evidenced constitutional faculty, even though it is not named explicitly as a distinct location in these two verses.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The character-level is the most directly evidenced constitutional location. All three verses locate semnotēs as a *character quality* — the stable property of the person's whole inner person that expresses itself comprehensively: "in every way" (1Ti2:2), "all dignity" (1Ti3:4), as a quality of teaching character (Tit2:7). The constitutional site is the character as a whole — the settled, comprehensive disposition of the inner person that shapes all their social expression — rather than a specific soul-faculty (heart, mind, will).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The will is the most directly evidenced soul-level faculty beyond the heart as an integrating location. 1Ch28:21 — "every willing man" — names the person by the orientation of their will (nadav = freely-willing); Exo35:5 — the "willing heart" is the heart whose will is freely-oriented. The will as distinct soul-level faculty is engaged and evidenced throughout the corpus even where the word "will" is not separately named.

---

##### T2.5.2 — If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The will as distinct soul-level location reveals that humility is not merely felt or understood but chosen and enacted. The repeated imperative form ("humble yourselves") addresses the person's capacity to initiate the act of self-lowering; the characteristic is not passively received but actively performed by the will. This reveals that humility, unlike conditions received from outside (such as comfort or peace), is fundamentally the person's own volitional contribution to their inner state — though it is also the appropriate response to divine initiative (the ka.na pattern, where God's word or judgment creates the occasion). The will is the constitutional faculty through which the person responds to divine address with the act of self-lowering.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The conscience as distinct soul-level location reveals that genuine submission has an *internal evaluative sustainer*: the person who genuinely submits does so not only from heart-orientation but from a conscience that has assessed the authority as legitimate and the submission as right. This is the difference between Phili2:12's sustained obedience (conscience-grounded, without external accountability) and mere social compliance (which cannot survive without external support). The conscience in this register is what makes submission resilient and sustainable — it internalises the authority's legitimacy and the submission's rightness so that neither requires constant external reinforcement.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

No additional soul-level location beyond heart and spirit is evidenced in §3.B. Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The will as the primary constitutional location reveals that meekness and gentleness are fundamentally volitional in their constitutional ground — not primarily emotional or cognitive but the quality and kinetics of the will itself. Metriopatheō (Heb5:2 — "can deal gently") names a volitional capacity; okneō (Act9:38) names volitional readiness. The will's quality — calibrated, non-hesitating — is the constitutional site of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The character as constitutional location reveals that semnotēs is a *comprehensively characterological* quality — it shapes the whole person's manner of inhabiting their existence rather than operating through a single faculty. 1Ti2:2 — "in every way" — the comprehensiveness confirms that the characteristic's constitutional reach is the whole character rather than a single internal faculty. This makes dignity one of the most broadly-reaching inner-being characteristics in M09: it is not located in one constitutional faculty but pervades the person's entire characterological being.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The will as distinct soul-level faculty reveals that willing-heartedness is constitutively volitional — it is the will's quality and direction (free, uncoerced) that defines the characteristic. The will in this characteristic is not the neutral capacity to choose but specifically the will in its freed, non-resistant, gladly-oriented posture toward God. The will's quality (willing vs unwilling) is the constitutional essence of the characteristic.

---

##### T2.5.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; will and affect are surfaced as distinct soul-level locations beyond heart and mind (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the conscience is evidenced as a distinct soul-level location (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on soul-level locations beyond spirit and heart (see T2.5.1). The characteristic's constitutional reach in this corpus is spirit-primary, heart-secondary.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The will is evidenced as a soul-level location (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2); other soul-level locations beyond the will are not evidenced in §3.C.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The character-level is evidenced as the primary constitutional location (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). Other specific soul-level locations (heart, mind, spirit) are not named in §3.D.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The will is evidenced as a soul-level location (see T2.5.1 and T2.5.2). Beyond will and heart: no additional soul-level locations are directly named in §3.E.

---

#### T2.6 — Body — Significance

##### T2.6.1 — Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Two body-part connexions appear. First, *weeping and tearing of clothes:* 2Ki22:19 and 2Ch34:27 both pair the inner act of humbling with the bodily expression of weeping and tearing clothes — these are the bodily signs that the inner humbling has genuinely occurred. Second, the body itself appears as the site of creaturely lowliness: Phili3:21 names the "lowly body" (sōma tēs tapeinōseōs) — the physical-creaturely body as the seat of the lowliness condition in M09-B. The body is not named as the location of the volitional act (M09-A) but as the location of the experienced creaturely condition (M09-B).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, in two forms. First, Rom6:12 — "let not sin reign in your mortal body, to make you obey its passions" — the body is named as the site of the competing submission: bodily passions are what sin's reign produces obedience to. The body is not the location of genuine submission but of its principal competition. Second, Eph6:5 — bodily service to earthly masters is the context within which the heart-located submission must operate — the outward bodily service is the expression of the inner submission. The body link is both competitive (Rom6:12 — bodily passions vs submission to God) and expressive (Eph6:5 — bodily service expressing inner submission).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not link contrition to a specific body part. The constitutional locations named are spirit and heart — inner-being faculties rather than physical body parts. The physical-resonance vocabulary (crushed, broken) is applied to the spirit and heart, not to a literal physical body part.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not link meekness or gentleness to a specific body part. Heb5:2's "beset with weakness" references creaturely bodily limitation generally rather than naming a specific body part.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not link semnotēs to a specific body part. The characteristic is an inner quality of character without specific body-part association.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The five-verse corpus does not link willing-heartedness to a specific body part. The constitutional locations named are heart and spirit — inner-being faculties rather than physical body parts. The outward acts (bringing gold, bringing offerings) involve bodily action but the characteristic itself is located in the heart and spirit, not in a named body part.

---

##### T2.6.2 — If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Two different functions are at work. The weeping/clothes-tearing link (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27) is *expressive*: the body expresses the genuine inner state, and God confirms he has heard (the inner act is the criterion, the bodily expression is its outward correlate). The emphasis is that genuine humbling has bodily expression — the body is not the site but the indicator. The Phili3:21 "lowly body" link is *indicative*: the body's creaturely lowliness points to the constitutional condition of the believer in the present age — mortal, suffering, lowly — which awaits its transformation. Here the body *is* the site of the condition rather than merely expressing it.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Two different functions. In Rom6:12, the link is *diagnostic*: the body's passions are named as the point of competition — submission to God versus submission to bodily desire are rival claims on the will. The body-link diagnoses where the competing submission operates and therefore where the battle for genuine submission must be fought. In Eph6:5, the link is *expressive*: the bodily service rendered to earthly masters is the outward form of the inner submission — the body-soul link here shows how inner submission necessarily takes outward form in the person's active conduct. Both functions confirm that the characteristic is not merely mental or spiritual but is engaged with the person's whole embodied existence.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

No body-part link is evidenced in §3.B (see T2.6.1). Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

No specific body-part link is evidenced in §3.C (see T2.6.1). Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

No body-part link is evidenced in §3.D. Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

No body-part link is evidenced in §3.E. Prompt closed.

---

##### T2.6.3 — If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced (see T2.6.1 and T2.6.2).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced (see T2.6.1 and T2.6.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-part links. The physical-resonance language (crushed, broken) describes inner constitutional states (spirit, heart) rather than literal physical body parts.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on specific body-part links. Heb5:2's reference to shared weakness is a creaturely-condition reference rather than a specific body-part link.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-part links for semnotēs. The characteristic's expression is through manner and comportment in social roles rather than through named body-part associations.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-part links. The characteristic's constitutional location is in the heart and spirit rather than in a named physical body part.

---

#### T2.7 — Body — Direction

##### T2.7.1 — Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to the soul, or does it run in both directions?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The direction differs between the two body-links identified in T2.6. For the weeping/clothes-tearing link (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27): the direction is *soul → body* — the inner act of humbling produces the bodily expression. God confirms he heard the inner act, not the bodily expression per se (though the bodily expression is the sign God cites — "you have torn your clothes and wept before me"). For the Phili3:21 "lowly body": the direction is ambiguous — the body's creaturely condition (M09-B experienced lowliness) is not produced by the inner disposition but is a given condition of creaturely existence. In this instance the direction is more complex: the body's state *shapes* the inner experience of lowliness (body → soul) rather than the soul expressing through the body.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The direction differs between the two body-links. In Rom6:12 (bodily passions — competition): the direction is *body → soul* in the negative direction — the body's passions exert a pull on the will, competing with the soul's submission to God. Sin's use of the body is the mechanism by which the competing submission operates: body → will's orientation. In Eph6:5 (bodily service — expression): the direction is *soul → body* — the genuine inner submission of the heart expresses itself through the bodily act of service. Heart → bodily conduct, with the heart's genuineness determining whether the bodily conduct is authentic (sincere heart as to Christ) or performative (eye-service).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

No body-characteristic link is evidenced in §3.B (see T2.6.1). This prompt is accordingly closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

No specific body-characteristic link is evidenced in §3.C. Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

No body-characteristic link evidenced. Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

No body-characteristic link evidenced. The constitutional movement is heart/spirit → outward act (bringing offerings), confirmed in T2.10, but no named body-part link is evidenced.

---

##### T2.7.2 — What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The soul→body direction (M09-A voluntary register) confirms that genuine humility is an inner act that finds outward expression — it cannot be reversed (outer expression generating inner humility) without the self-referential performance problem that Col2:23 identifies. The body→soul direction in M09-B (the creaturely lowliness condition shaping inner experience) reveals that humility in its condition-register is partly constituted by the bodily-creaturely situation — the person who is genuinely low in estate cannot escape the experience through inner assertion alone. This directionality distinction helps clarify why the two sub-groups (M09-A voluntary, M09-B experienced) have different operational profiles: M09-A is primarily inner → outer; M09-B involves a body → inner dimension.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The bidirectionality reveals that submission is engaged in a genuine body-soul interaction. The soul → body direction (Eph6:5) shows that genuine inner submission necessarily expresses itself outwardly — submission that produces no outer conduct is suspect. The body → soul direction (Rom6:12) shows that the body's passions are a genuine constitutional force competing with the soul's submission to God — the body is not neutral territory. The characteristic must be held at the soul/will level against the bodily-passion pull (Rom6:12), while also flowing into and expressing through bodily conduct (Eph6:5). This confirms submission as engaging the whole person, not merely the inner life in isolation.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

No body-characteristic link is evidenced; direction cannot be analysed. The characteristic operates at spirit and heart level without a named body-part correlate in this corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

No body-characteristic link evidenced; direction cannot be analysed.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

No body-characteristic link evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

No body-characteristic link evidenced. Prompt closed.

---

##### T2.7.3 — If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Body links are evidenced and the direction is analysed (see T2.7.1 and T2.7.2).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Body links are evidenced and the direction analysed (see T2.7.1 and T2.7.2).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-characteristic links (see T2.6.1 and T2.7.1). All constitutional locations named are inner-being rather than bodily.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-characteristic links for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-characteristic links for semnotēs.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The evidence is silent on body-characteristic links for this characteristic.

---

#### T2.8 — Body — Deposit

##### T2.8.1 — Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The evidence corpus for Humility (CHAR-1) does not directly evidence a constitutional deposit in the body from sustained operation of the characteristic. The Phili3:21 evidence names the current bodily lowliness as a condition awaiting transformation, not as the deposit of sustained humility. The weeping expressions (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27) are momentary bodily expressions, not deposits. The characteristic's effects evidenced in the corpus are characterological and relational (wisdom, contentment, community harmony, divine favour — see T1.6.1), not identified as bodily deposits. This silence is analytically significant: humility appears to deposit primarily in character and relational capacity rather than constitutionally in the body.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The Submission corpus does not directly evidence a constitutional deposit in the body from sustained operation of the characteristic. Rom6:17 ("obedience from the heart") and 1Pe1:22 ("purifying the soul") locate the deposits in the heart and soul respectively, not in the body. The body is named as a site of competition (Rom6:12) rather than of deposit from submission.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence a constitutional deposit in the body from sustained contrition. The characteristic's operation is evidenced at spirit and heart level; God's reviving response (Isa57:15) produces constitutional renewal at those same levels. No bodily deposit is named.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence a constitutional deposit in the body from sustained meekness and gentleness. The characteristic's constitutional location is in the will and inner person; no bodily deposit is named.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not evidence a constitutional bodily deposit from sustained semnotēs. The characteristic's sustained effects are social-ordering and character-expressive rather than bodily deposit.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The five-verse corpus does not evidence a constitutional bodily deposit from sustained willing-heartedness. The characteristic's sustained effects are in the heart/spirit and in the outward acts of generous giving/service.

---

##### T2.8.2 — What evidence supports or contradicts this?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

No verse in the Humility corpus directly contradicts the absence of bodily deposit. The closest potential evidence is the cultivated contentment of Phili4:12 ("I have learned the secret") — suggesting that repeated exposure to the lowliness condition produces a learned inner stability, but the locus is characterological (the inner person's learned disposition) rather than bodily. No verse affirms generational consequence or bodily deposit of sustained humility.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

No verse in §3.A directly contradicts the absence of bodily deposit. The characteristic's deposits are characterological and soul-level (1Pe1:22 — soul-purification; love from a pure heart). No verse affirms generational consequence or bodily deposit from sustained submission in this corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

No evidence in §3.B supports or contradicts bodily deposit from sustained contrition. The characteristic's sustained effects (reviving of spirit and heart) are at the inner constitutional level, not evidenced as bodily deposit.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

No evidence in §3.C supports or contradicts bodily deposit. The characteristic's effects are inner-quality-based rather than bodily-deposit-based within this corpus.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

No evidence in §3.D supports or contradicts bodily deposit from semnotēs. The characteristic's expression is in manner and character-quality rather than in bodily deposits.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

No evidence in §3.E supports or contradicts bodily deposit. The characteristic's deposits are characterological (habitual generosity) rather than bodily.

---

##### T2.8.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit from sustained humility. This finding feeds directly into T5.7, which will note the same and close that prompt accordingly.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit from sustained submission. This feeds into T5.7, which will note the same and close accordingly.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit. This feeds into T5.7, which will note the same and close accordingly.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit. This feeds into T5.7 which will close accordingly.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit. This feeds into T5.7 which will close accordingly.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional bodily deposit. This feeds into T5.7 which will close accordingly.

---

#### T2.9 — Origin and Source

##### T2.9.1 — Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The corpus evidences multiple origins, varying by register. *Generated from within (M09-A voluntary):* the dominant pattern in M09-A is the person generating the act of humbling from within — "humble yourselves" (Jam4:10; 1Pe5:6) addresses the volitional capacity to initiate. The person is the constitutional origin of the act. *Occasioned by divine address:* in the ka.na corpus (2Ch34:27; 2Ki22:19; 2Ch36:12), the trigger for the inner act of humbling is hearing God's word — the origin is divine address that awakens the inner response. The humbling is generated within but requires the external occasion of divine speech. *Imposed from without (M09-B):* in the imposed-lowering instances (2Ch28:19; Psa107:12), God is the agent and the humbling originates externally — it is not the person's own act but God's action on them. The characteristic thus has at least three constitutional origins depending on the register: person-generated, divinely-occasioned, and divinely-imposed.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The corpus evidences multiple constitutional origins varying by register. *Person-generated (volitional):* Gal2:5 (Paul deliberately withholds submission — the will's own act); Heb11:8 (Abraham obeyed by faith — the volitional inner response to divine call); Phili2:12 (sustained without external support — the will generating from within). *Faith-enabled (divinely-occasioned):* obedience of faith (Rom1:5; 16:26; Heb11:8) — the characteristic is the will's response to God's word and gospel, so God's address occasions the response. *Spirit-directed (divinely-produced):* 1Pe1:2 — "in the sanctification of the Spirit, for obedience to Jesus Christ" — the Spirit's sanctifying work produces and directs the inner orientation of will toward Christ. *Formed through suffering:* Heb5:8 — Christ's obedience was learned through what he suffered — the characteristic is formed through costly engagement, not merely chosen or bestowed.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The corpus implies a complex origin. The characteristic arises from the encounter between the person's moral reality and God's holiness — it is occasioned rather than self-generated. Isa57:15 — the high-and-holy God who names his dwelling with the contrite implies that his holy presence is the occasioning reality that produces the contrite response. The crushing (dak.ka) suggests the characteristic results from a process — something acting on the person's inner constitution (moral failure confronted, or divine holiness encountered) rather than something the person generates independently. The origin is thus *relational-occasioned*: the characteristic arises at the intersection of the person's own moral condition and their encounter with divine holiness.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 evidences the constitutional origin directly: metriopatheō is grounded in and originates from the genuine inner awareness of one's own shared creaturely weakness ("since he himself is beset with weakness" — kathoti causal). The origin is *self-knowledge of shared creaturely limitation* that translates into compassionate calibrated restraint toward others in similar limitation. This is a complex origin: the characteristic is generated by the intersection of (a) genuine inner self-awareness of one's own weakness and (b) the encounter with others who are in weakness or waywardness. Act9:38's okneō is evidenced as an expected quality without naming its specific constitutional origin beyond the general volitional capacity for readiness.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The corpus does not directly address the constitutional origin of semnotēs, but its expression as a character quality shaped by the person's godliness (1Ti2:2 — paired with eusebeia) and integrity (Tit2:7 — alongside integrity) suggests it originates in the intersection of genuine godliness and authentic moral character. The characteristic is produced by genuine inner formation rather than social acquisition — 1Ti3:4's "with all dignity" as a standard for leadership suggests it is the fruit of genuine characterological formation. The origin is constitutionally characterological — emerging from the whole-person formation that godliness and integrity produce.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The corpus evidences two origins by register. *VCG-01 (self-generated):* the characteristic originates from within the person — "whoever is of a generous/willing heart" (Exo35:5) — the heart's own free movement is the origin. The freely-moving heart generates the characteristic from within rather than receiving it from outside. *VCG-02 (divinely-given):* Psa51:12 — "uphold me with a willing spirit" — the characteristic must be divinely given and sustained after failure; the origin after moral failure is God's upholding rather than the person's self-generation. The origins are thus both inner-generated (VCG-01) and divinely-given (VCG-02).

---

##### T2.9.2 — What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The origin is multiple, as T2.9.1 demonstrates. The structural distinction between M09-A and M09-B maps precisely onto this plurality: M09-A (voluntary) is primarily person-generated and divinely-occasioned; M09-B (imposed) is primarily divinely-imposed or circumstantially-generated. Within M09-A, the Colossian material (Col2:18; Col2:23) adds a fourth origin-variant: humility can be *performed* — generated from a false origin (self-referential asceticism) rather than from genuine inner transformation. The genuine characteristic must originate from the heart's actual response to God and to others, not from a self-constructed discipline that keeps the self at the centre.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The origin is clearly multiple, as T2.9.1 demonstrates. The most significant tension within the multiple origins is between the Spirit-directed (1Pe1:2 — Spirit produces it) and the person-generated (Phili2:12 — "work out your own salvation with fear and trembling") registers. Phili2:13 (outside this corpus but structurally implied by Phili2:12's context — "for it is God who works in you both to will and to work") would resolve this tension as a both-and: God works; the person works. The corpus evidence alone (Phili2:12 — the human command; 1Pe1:2 — the Spirit's direction) presents both origins without contradiction, implying the characteristic's origin is jointly human-volitional and Spirit-enabled.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The two-verse corpus suggests the origin is constituted by at least two factors: (1) the person's own moral condition (the failure or limitation that occasions the breaking); and (2) the encounter with divine holiness or truth (Isa57:15 — the high-and-holy One's self-disclosure as the frame within which the contrite spirit is named). Both factors together constitute the origin: the characteristic arises when the person's moral reality is confronted in the light of God's holiness, and neither factor alone is sufficient.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 evidences a multiple origin: the characteristic requires both the self-knowledge of one's own weakness AND the encounter with the erring other's condition. Neither alone is sufficient: self-awareness without the erring other produces nothing; encounter with the erring without self-awareness produces severity rather than gentleness. The origin is the relational conjunction of the two.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The evidence suggests multiple contributing origins: genuine godliness (1Ti2:2 — paired with eusebeia), integrity (Tit2:7 — listed alongside integrity), and characterological formation that produces the gravity appropriate to leadership roles (1Ti3:4). The characteristic arises from the convergence of these forming influences rather than a single constitutional source.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The origin is multiple, as T2.9.1 demonstrates: the characteristic originates both from within (the freely-moving heart of VCG-01) and from God (the divinely-upheld willing spirit of VCG-02). The most significant insight is that these two origins are not contradictory but complementary: the self-generated willing-heartedness of VCG-01 is the natural expression of the genuine inner orientation; the divinely-given willing spirit of VCG-02 is the same characteristic requiring divine restoration and sustaining after the inner orientation has been disrupted by moral failure.

---

##### T2.9.3 — Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, the origin changes consistently with context. In individual crisis-response contexts (the ka.na narrative — Manasseh in 2Ch33:12, Josiah in 2Ch34:27), the origin is the person's own volitional response to acute divine pressure. In community contexts (2Ch12:6 — the princes and king humble themselves corporately; 2Ch30:11 — men from Asher and Manasseh), the origin involves both individual will and communal movement. In the apostolic/Christological vocation context (Act20:19; Phili2:8), the origin is located in the person's sustained volitional character. In the M09-B imposed contexts (2Ch28:19; Psa107:12), the origin is purely divine action. The Pauline epistolary context (Col3:12; Eph4:2) presents humility as a deliberately chosen character-garment — origin in the renewed-person's volitional character formation. Each context generates a somewhat different origin profile.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes. *Acute-event context* (Heb11:8 — Abraham's obedient departure): faith-driven volitional response to a specific divine command. *Sustained-community context* (Phili2:12 — "always obeyed"): volitional disposition sustained by conscience and fear of God across time. *Formative-costly context* (Heb5:8 — Christ learning obedience through suffering): the characteristic acquired through costly engagement rather than immediately present. *Eschatological-gospel context* (Rom1:5; 16:26): the Spirit's work producing the nations' obedience as the telos of gospel proclamation. Each context evidences a somewhat different origin profile — crisis-faith, sustained-conscience, costly-formation, Spirit-telos — confirming the plurality of origin across contexts.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus is too thin to evidence context-dependent variation in the origin. Both verses evidence the same origin structure: inner brokenness in relation to God. Broader canonical investigation would be needed to assess whether the origin varies (e.g., contrition produced by prophetic address vs personal moral awakening vs worship encounter with God's holiness), but §3.B alone does not provide that evidence.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence context-dependent variation in the origin. Both terms have a consistent origin structure (self-awareness enabling calibrated response; volitional readiness enabling prompt response) without contextual variation evidenced within these two verses.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not evidence context-dependent variation in the origin. The same semnotēs appears across three contexts (public life, household, teaching) as the consistent expression of the same character quality, suggesting a single stable origin rather than context-dependent variation.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes, context-dependently as T2.9.1 evidences. In the community-worship contexts (Exo35; 1Ch28:21; 2Ch29:31): the origin is the person's own freely-moved heart — a natural inner expression. In the penitential context (Psa51:12): the origin is divine upholding — the characteristic must be received from God because the person's own capacity has been disrupted. The origin thus shifts from inner-generated (person at peace with God) to divinely-restored (person after moral failure), while the characteristic itself remains the same inner quality across both registers.

#### T2.10 — Constitutional Movement

##### T2.10.1 — Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (G)

The AI session omitted T2.10.{1,2,3} from the M09 CHAR-1 findings file (3 prompts missing of 189). Placeholder gap inserted by CC to preserve cluster_finding row integrity. Researcher to revisit at Session C or audit time; the substantive T2.x findings (T2.1 through T2.9 + T2.11) are present and may provide adjacent evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes. The clearest constitutional movement is evidenced in 1Pe1:22: *truth → obedience → soul-purification → sincere brotherly love from a pure heart*. The movement: the person hears and submits to truth (volitional-heart level) → the soul itself is purified (soul-level transformation) → the affective capacity of love is produced in the heart (affective-heart level). This evidences a downward constitutional movement: from will-engagement to soul-transformation to heart-affective production. Rom6:12–17 evidences an upward movement in the competitive sense: bodily passions → will's yielding → determination of whose servant one is. The characteristic moves across constitutional levels in both its formative and competitive dimensions.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes. Isa57:15 evidences a constitutional movement in God's reviving response: "to revive the spirit of the lowly, and to revive the heart of the contrite" — the reviving moves from spirit to heart (or addresses both simultaneously). The characteristic itself is located at both spirit and heart level (Psa34:18; Isa57:15), suggesting it operates across both rather than being confined to one. The crushing appears to begin at the spirit level (ruach crushed) and affect the heart-level as well (brokenhearted — Psa34:18). Constitutional movement: spirit → heart in the characteristic's own operation; and God's reviving movement mirrors this (reviving spirit and heart — Isa57:15).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes, in the direction from inner-to-outer. Metriopatheō (Heb5:2) — the inner capacity for measured compassionate restraint expresses itself outwardly in the manner of engagement with the erring ("deal gently with the ignorant and wayward"). The movement is inner capacity → outward manner of engagement. Okneō (Act9:38) — the inner volitional readiness expresses itself in the outward act of immediate responsive movement ("come to us without delay"). Both evidence the inner quality moving into outward expression without naming the constitutional sequence across specific inner levels.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes, from inner quality to outward expression. The characteristic is inner (a quality of character) expressing outward (in the manner of inhabiting public life, household leadership, and teaching). 1Ti3:4 — the overseer's dignity produces orderly compliance in his children — the inner character quality moves outward to produce ordered relational effects. The constitutional movement is *inner character → outward relational ordering*.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes. The constitutional movement is: *heart/spirit (inner willing disposition) → outward acts (bringing offerings, skilled service)*. Exo35:5 — "of a willing heart, let him bring" — the bringing flows from the heart. Exo35:22 — "all who were of a willing heart brought" — inner disposition → outer act. 1Ch28:21 — "every willing man who has skill" — the inner willing enables the outer skilled participation. Psa51:12 — the willing spirit as the precondition for "joyful, freely-offered devotion" — spirit → devotional engagement. The movement is consistently inner → outer.

---

##### T2.10.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (G)

Omitted by AI session; placeholder gap (see T2.10.1).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The pattern from 1Pe1:22 is sequential: (1) hearing truth / encounter with authority's claim; (2) volitional act of submission (heart-level); (3) soul-purification through sustained obedience; (4) affective production (sincere love from pure heart). The movement is top-down in the constitutional sense (will → soul → affect), with the will's act initiating a transformation that reaches constitutional levels below the initiating act. The Rom6:12 competitive pattern is bottom-up: body's passions → will's yielding → allegiance-orientation. These two movement patterns (initiated at will-level going downward into soul; initiated at body-level going upward to will) confirm that the characteristic is caught between competing constitutional movements and must be actively maintained at the will-level.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The sequence implied by the two verses together: (1) the spirit is crushed (Psa34:18 — dak.ka-ruach); (2) the heart is broken (Psa34:18 — nishbar-lev); (3) God draws near and saves (Psa34:18); (4) God dwells with the contrite spirit (Isa57:15); (5) God revives both spirit and heart (Isa57:15). The constitutional movement is: crushing at spirit-level → breaking at heart-level → divine nearness → divine reviving of spirit and heart. The pattern is: the characteristic descends into the person constitutionally (spirit then heart), and God's reviving ascends through the same constitutional pathway (spirit and heart both revived).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The pattern evidenced is: *inner quality/capacity → outward manner of engagement or movement*. Metriopatheō: inner calibrated compassion → gentle outward dealing. Okneō: inner volitional freedom-from-hesitation → immediate outward response. The constitutional movement is soul/will → outward expression, with the inner quality determining the character of the outward act. No further constitutional sequence within the inner levels is evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The pattern across the three verses is consistent: *inner character quality (semnotēs) → ordered outward expression in social roles*. 1Ti2:2: inner dignity → peaceful public life. 1Ti3:4: inner dignity → orderly household governance. Tit2:7: inner dignity → authenticated teaching. In each case the outward ordering or authentication flows from the inner quality — it is upstream and the outward expression is downstream. The movement is consistently *character → expression* rather than *expression → character*.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The pattern across the corpus is: *inner willing disposition (heart/spirit) → immediate outer act without friction*. The movement is characterised by the absence of hesitation — the willing heart brings; the willing spirit enables joyful devotion. There is no evidence of a mediating stage between the inner disposition and the outer act. The constitutional movement is direct and unimpeded: inner willing → outer expression, with no resistance stage. This distinguishes willing-heartedness from characteristics that require more mediation between inner state and outer expression.

---

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (G)

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

### T3

#### T3.1 — Perception

##### T3.1.1 — Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, through the *hearing* inner sense. The ka.na corpus consistently shows the humbling triggered by hearing God's word: 2Ki22:19 — "when you heard how I spoke against this place"; 2Ch34:27 — "when you heard his words against this place"; 2Ch36:12 — Zedekiah refused to humble himself "before Jeremiah the prophet, who spoke from the mouth of the Lord." The act of genuine hearing — taking the spoken divine word as personally addressed — is the perceptive event that enables the inner response of humbling. The perceptive faculty is not merely the external ear but the inner hearing that receives God's word as genuinely claiming. In the NT register, Mat11:29 invites learning — "learn from me" — which engages the inner hearing and seeing of the self relative to Christ's example.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, primarily through *inner hearing*. The Greek root of hupakoē — hupo + akouō (under-hearing) — makes the auditory-perceptive function etymologically central. Genuine submission requires hearing the authority's claim as genuinely addressed to oneself. The gospel-obedience cluster (M09-D-VCG-01) is constituted by the reception of the word: Rom10:16 — "they have not all obeyed the gospel" is explained by the implicit hearing-without-yielding (quoting "who has believed what he has heard from us") — the gap between hearing and obeying is the gap between outer reception and inner submission. Gen49:10 and Pro30:17 (the OT obedience terms) also operate in contexts of hearing and responding to a word of authority. The characteristic is constitutively auditory in its engagement with the perceptive faculty.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, through *spiritual discernment* — the inner capacity to perceive one's moral reality before God. Both verses evidence a person who has genuinely perceived their own broken condition (Psa34:18 — brokenhearted; Isa57:15 — contrite in spirit). This perception of moral reality before divine holiness is an act of the inner perceptive faculty at its deepest level. Isa57:15's framing — the high-and-holy God naming his dwelling with the contrite — implies that the contrite person has perceived God's holiness in a way that has crushed their self-sufficiency.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes. Metriopatheō (Heb5:2) requires perceiving the other's condition accurately — the high priest must perceive that the person is "ignorant and wayward" in order to engage with appropriate calibrated gentleness rather than severity. The perceptive faculty is engaged in the accurate reading of the other's inner-being condition that enables the calibrated response. Additionally, the grounding in "shared weakness" requires the high priest to perceive his own creaturely limitation accurately — genuine perception of shared condition, not self-deceived superiority. Act9:38's okneō engages perception in the sense of immediately recognising the genuine urgency of the call without hesitating to assess whether it warrants response.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs engages perception through the *manner in which one is perceived* by others — 1Ti3:4 (dignity producing orderly compliance in children) and Tit2:7 (dignity authenticating teaching) both evidence that the characteristic affects how others perceive and respond to the person. From the person's own perceptive side: possessing genuine semnotēs requires accurately perceiving what is appropriate gravity for one's role and context — the calibration of the characteristic to "in every way" (1Ti2:2) requires accurate perception of the relational and social context.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The perceptive faculty is engaged through the person's recognition of the call and the genuine need for response. Exo35:5 — "take from among you a contribution to the Lord. Whoever is of a generous heart, let him bring" — Moses's announcement is heard, and the willing-hearted person perceives it as genuinely calling for their free response. The perceptive faculty enables the willing person to receive the call as genuinely directed to their inner freedom rather than as external compulsion.
