The willing-hearted person is one who perceives the invitation and responds from within; the unwilling person may perceive the same call but not experience the inner free movement toward it.

---

##### T3.1.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *enables and deepens* the perceptive faculty. Pro11:2 — "with the humble is wisdom" — and the consistent pattern of God confirming he heard the humbling person (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27) together suggest that the humble person's inner receptivity allows genuine perception of divine address and of reality. By contrast, the non-humbling person (2Ch36:12 — Zedekiah) is evidenced as closed to the prophet's word — the perceptive faculty is impaired by the absence of humility. Col2:18 (the person puffed up by the "sensuous mind") shows that pride distorts rather than enables genuine perception. Humility, as the inner openness that does not close itself to external reality, actively enables the perceptive faculty to function without the distortion of self-referential protection.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *enables and deepens* genuine reception of what is heard. Rom10:16 evidences that hearing without inner yielding is a deficient reception — the perceptive faculty hears but does not receive at the level required. Genuine submission enables the word heard to penetrate to the soul-level (1Pe1:22 — "obedience to the truth" purifying the soul). Conversely, the inner refusal that characterises non-submission (2Th3:14 — inner refusal revealed by failure to obey) impairs the perceptive reception of the authority's word — the person hears but closes against the claim. Submission thus enables the perceptive faculty's full function (hearing + yielding to what is heard) rather than its partial function (hearing + resisting).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *presupposes and deepens* the perceptive faculty. The characteristic cannot exist without a genuine inner perception of moral reality (the person must genuinely perceive their own failure or God's holiness). Conversely, the person whose perceptive faculty is distorted by pride or self-justification cannot arrive at genuine contrition — the blocking of genuine perception blocks the characteristic's formation. Contrition thus presupposes a functioning inner perception of moral reality and deepens it by validating the perception as accurate rather than allowing the self-protective deflection that would prevent it.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Meekness/gentleness *enables and deepens* genuine perception of others' conditions. The self-knowledge of shared weakness (Heb5:2) that grounds metriopatheō enables the person to perceive others' conditions with recognition rather than condemnation — the gentle person sees the erring through the lens of their own limitation and therefore perceives more accurately (without the distortion of assumed superiority). Conversely, the prideful assumption of superiority impairs genuine perception of the erring other's condition — severity replaces the perceptive empathy that shared-weakness awareness provides.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *enables accurate social perception* in others — the person of dignity is perceived clearly rather than through the distorting lens of ostentatious self-display or frivolousness. 1Ti3:4 — the orderly compliance the overseer's dignity produces implies children perceive the genuine authority-weight of the parent clearly. Tit2:7 — teaching authenticated by dignity enables hearers to perceive its content as genuinely weighty. The characteristic thus enables others' perceptive faculty to receive the person's authority and instruction without distortion.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *enables genuine reception* of the invitation to give. The freely-moved heart (Exo35:5/22) receives the call with openness rather than resistance — the perceptive faculty receives the call without the filtering of reluctance that the un-willing heart would impose. Psa51:12's request for a willing spirit implies that without it, the person cannot genuinely receive the possibility of joyful devotion — the burdened, not-yet-restored spirit perceives but cannot freely receive. Willing-heartedness thus enables the perceptive faculty to receive invitations to giving and service without the filtering of reluctance.

---

##### T3.1.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The pattern reveals that humility is constitutively *receptive*: the characteristic is the inner posture that allows genuine perception because it does not interpose the self's self-protective distortions between the person and what is genuinely real. The proud person (Zedekiah in 2Ch36:12; the Col2:18 person) cannot genuinely hear because their self-enclosure filters incoming reality through the lens of self-preservation. The humble person (Josiah in 2Ch34:27; Paul in Act20:19) is genuinely open to being addressed, corrected, and informed. Humility is thus not merely one characteristic among others but a structural enabler of perceptive functioning — the inner condition without which the person cannot genuinely hear God or others.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The auditory-perceptive pattern reveals that submission is constitutively *responsive*: it cannot originate from the person alone but requires something heard — a word, a command, a gospel claim — to which the will yields. This confirms that submission is a *relational-responsive* characteristic rather than a self-generated one: it is the inner side of the person's response to a genuine address from a legitimate authority. The hupakoē root makes this permanent: submission is, at its root, "hearing-under" — the will that receives and yields rather than deflects or resists.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals that contrition is constitutively epistemic at its ground: it requires genuine inner seeing of what is true about oneself before God. The person who is genuinely contrite is one who has seen accurately — their spirit crushed by what genuine moral self-knowledge before divine holiness reveals. This makes contrition a characteristic that cannot be faked at the perceptive level: genuine crushing requires genuine perception of the reality that occasions it.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The pattern reveals that metriopatheō (Heb5:2) depends on a double perceptive act: (a) accurate perception of one's own creaturely limitation; and (b) accurate perception of the other's wayward condition through the lens of that shared limitation. The characteristic thus deepens perception by requiring it to be both self-directed and other-directed simultaneously — the gentle person is one who genuinely sees both themselves and others with the same accuracy that shared human experience enables.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The pattern reveals that semnotēs operates partly through others' perception of the person's settled gravity — it is not merely an inner state but one that produces a perceptual field around the person in which genuine authority and authenticity can be received. The characteristic thus has an outward-perceptual dimension: it shapes how others receive the person's presence, instruction, and authority by providing a clear, undistorted signal of settled moral gravity.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The pattern reveals that willing-heartedness determines whether the call to free giving is received as invitation or experienced as burden. The willing-hearted person (Exo35:5/22) perceives the call as an opportunity for free expression; the person whose spirit is not yet willing (Psa51:12 — pre-restoration) perceives the same call as an obligation they cannot freely fulfil. The characteristic thus shapes the perceptive faculty's reception of calls to giving and service.

---

#### T3.2 — Cognition

##### T3.2.1 — Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, and extensively. Pro11:2 directly links humility to wisdom as its cognitive companion: "with the humble is wisdom." Phili2:3 defines humility as a cognitive act — "count others more significant than yourselves" — using hēgeomai (to reckon, consider, evaluate). This cognitive dimension is not peripheral but central to the definition: genuine humility requires an accurate cognitive assessment of relative worth that re-orders the self's self-assessment. Col2:18 evidences the distorted cognitive state that false humility produces: the "sensuous mind" that is puffed up, revealing that genuine humility requires cognitive realism rather than self-inflated assessment. Mat11:29 ("learn from me") frames humility as itself an educational-cognitive process.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, directly and explicitly. 2Cor10:5 — "take every thought captive to obey Christ" — the cognitive faculty (every thought, noēma) is the battleground. The "arguments and every lofty opinion raised against the knowledge of God" are cognitive constructs that submission must overcome. The cognitive faculty is engaged as both the site of resistance (proud reasoning) and the domain where submission must be established (cognitive allegiance to Christ). Additionally, the discernment required to distinguish legitimate from illegitimate authority (Gal2:5 — Paul deliberately withholding submission) is a cognitive-evaluative function that submission requires.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, indirectly. Genuine contrition requires genuine cognitive self-assessment — the accurate knowledge of one's failure or limitation before God. Without a cognitive grasp of the moral reality (what has occurred, why it matters before God's holiness), the characteristic cannot be genuine. However, the two-verse corpus does not name the mind or cognitive faculty explicitly; the cognitive engagement is implied by the nature of the characteristic rather than directly evidenced in the text of these two verses.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes. The self-assessment of shared weakness (Heb5:2 — "he himself is beset with weakness") requires a genuine cognitive recognition of one's own creaturely limitation — not merely an emotional sense of weakness but a clear cognitive understanding of one's shared condition with those who err. Metriopatheō's "measured" quality (metrios) also implies cognitive calibration: the person must cognitively assess what measure of engagement is appropriate to the erring person's condition, neither excessive nor insufficient.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs engages the cognitive faculty in the self-assessment dimension: genuine possession of the characteristic requires accurately assessing what is appropriate gravity for one's role and context (the comprehensiveness of "in every way" in 1Ti2:2 and "all dignity" in 1Ti3:4 implies an ongoing cognitive calibration). Tit2:7 — dignity alongside integrity authenticating teaching — implies that the teacher must cognitively maintain the connection between inner character and outward instruction, ensuring consistency.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The cognitive faculty is engaged in the assessment of what to give and how to serve: 1Ch28:21 — "every willing man who has skill for any kind of service" — the willingness operates alongside skill (cognitive-technical competence) rather than replacing it. The willing person brings their cognitive skill to the service rather than operating without cognitive engagement. The characteristic does not bypass the cognitive faculty but enables its wholehearted engagement rather than its reluctant or partial participation.

---

##### T3.2.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *enables and deepens* genuine cognition. Pro11:2 establishes the enabling connexion: the humble possess wisdom, the proud gain disgrace — the cognitive capacity for genuine understanding is linked to the posture of humility. This is consistent with the perceptive pattern (T3.1.2): the self-enclosure of pride distorts cognition, while the openness of humility enables accurate perception and therefore accurate understanding. The Colossian critique of false humility (Col2:18) shows that distorted self-assessment (cognitive pride operating within an outwardly humble practice) impairs rather than enables genuine understanding. Genuine humility enables cognition by removing the self-protective filter that keeps the person from accurately knowing themselves, God, and others.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *rightly orders and deepens* genuine cognition. Taking every thought captive to Christ (2Cor10:5) is not the suppression of thinking but its reorientation under a legitimate authority — it enables more accurate cognition by placing it under a reliable epistemic authority (Christ) rather than leaving it to self-generated "lofty opinions." Rom16:19 — Paul redirects the Romans' obedient disposition toward "wisdom as to what is good" — submission enables the discernment that pure self-generated reasoning cannot produce. The absence of genuine submission is linked to cognitive self-deception: the "lofty opinions" of 2Cor10:5 are the cognitive dysfunction that resists the knowledge of God.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *enables accurate cognition* of one's moral condition. The person in genuine contrition is one who has arrived at a truthful cognitive assessment of their own failure — the breaking is, in part, the cognitive-experiential event of genuine self-knowledge before God. The characteristic deepens cognitive honesty by validating it: the person who genuinely confronts their failure rather than defending against it is engaging the cognitive faculty most accurately. The structural opposite (self-justification, pride, hardening) impairs accurate moral cognition by distorting the person's self-assessment.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Meekness/gentleness *enables more accurate cognition* of others' conditions by removing the distorting lens of assumed superiority. The high priest who genuinely knows his own weakness (Heb5:2) cognises the erring other's condition more accurately — without the distortions that self-protective pride introduces. The characteristic thus deepens the cognitive capacity for accurate social and moral perception by grounding it in genuine self-knowledge.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *deepens credible cognition* in the teaching and leadership registers. Tit2:7 — teaching authenticated by dignity — enables hearers to receive the instruction as genuinely credible, enhancing their cognitive reception of the content. The characteristic enables the cognitive function of teaching to be received as weighty rather than dismissed as ungrounded performance.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *enables wholehearted cognitive engagement*. 1Ch28:21 — "every willing man who has skill" — willingness enables the full deployment of skill; the unwilling would bring their skill under compulsion without genuine engagement. The characteristic enables the cognitive faculty to be applied with genuine investment rather than with the distracted half-engagement of reluctant compliance.

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The cognitive engagement reveals that humility is, in part, an *epistemic virtue*: the character-disposition that enables accurate knowing. Pro11:2 is the summary statement; the broader corpus confirms it — Ahab's humbling (1Ki21:29) involves genuine acknowledgment of his situation before God; Josiah's humbling (2Ch34:27) involves receiving God's word as accurate address to his situation; the tax collector's humbling (Luk18:14) involves accurate self-knowledge before God ("be merciful to me, a sinner" — outside this corpus but the same register). Humility enables the person to know what is genuinely true about themselves and their situation, which is the prerequisite for genuine wisdom.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The pattern reveals that submission and cognition have a genuine reciprocal relationship: genuine submission enables more accurate cognition (by reorienting it under Christ's authority and producing wisdom, Rom16:19); and accurate cognition is required for submission (discerning legitimate authority, Gal2:5; taking thoughts captive as a deliberate cognitive act, 2Cor10:5). The characteristic is not anti-cognitive but rather requires and enables the cognitive faculty to function at its best — under legitimate authority rather than in self-generated autonomy.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that contrition is grounded in a cognitive act of moral self-knowledge even while it is primarily an affective-existential state. The characteristic requires cognitive honesty as a precondition — without it, the crushing cannot be genuine (mere emotional breakdown without cognitive moral self-knowledge is not contrition in the biblical sense). This makes cognition a secondary but necessary faculty: the characteristic is primarily affective-existential (T1.8.1) but requires and validates accurate moral cognition as its ground.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that metriopatheō (Heb5:2) is an *epistemically enabling* characteristic — it grounds more accurate cognition of others' conditions by requiring prior accurate cognition of one's own. The calibrated quality of the engagement (measured/metrios) requires cognitive assessment of what is proportionate; the shared-weakness ground requires cognitive honest self-assessment. The characteristic thus requires and enables genuine cognitive functioning rather than bypassing it.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The pattern reveals that semnotēs enables the cognitive reception of authority and teaching by providing the character-ground that authenticates content. Where the characteristic is absent (in teaching or leadership), the cognitive content may be rejected not on its merits but because the character-ground that would make it credible is lacking (Tit2:7 implies this — dignity as authenticating quality).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The pattern reveals that willing-heartedness enables genuine cognitive investment rather than mere presence — the 1Ch28:21 pairing of willingness with skill implies that genuine skilled service requires willing-heartedness as its motivational ground. Without the inner willing disposition, the cognitive skill is present but not fully engaged; with it, the cognitive faculty operates in wholehearted integrated service.

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Memory engagement is implicit rather than explicit in the corpus. The ka.na narrative pattern (Israel's repeated failures and humblings across Chronicles) suggests that the absence of humility involves a failure of moral memory — not retaining the lessons of prior judgment. 2Ch33:19 records Manasseh's humbling as a "turning point" in his biography, suggesting the memory-function of marking and retaining the significance of an inner event. However, the corpus does not directly name the memory faculty as engaged by humility. The clearest implicit memory connexion is 2Ch33:23 (Amon's failure to humble as Manasseh his father had) — the comparison implies that Manasseh's example was available as a remembered model which Amon refused to follow.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Memory engagement is present but implicit. 2Cor7:15 — Titus's "deepened affection" is stirred by "recalling the Corinthians' obedience" — the memory of the community's past obedience functions as the affective prompt for renewed relation. Phile21 — Paul's confidence in Philemon's obedience is based on a known track-record (a memory-informed character assessment). The characteristic's sustained formation (Phili2:12 — "always obeyed") implies a memory-function in tracking the consistency of the inner disposition across time.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the memory faculty. Psa34:18 and Isa57:15 address the present state of contrition and God's response to it without naming memory as an engaged faculty.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the memory faculty. The shared-weakness ground of Heb5:2 may implicitly involve the memory of one's own past failures or experiences of weakness, but this is inferred beyond the text.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the memory faculty by semnotēs. The characteristic is addressed as a present character quality without memory-function engagement named.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The five-verse corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the memory faculty. Psa51:12's penitential context implies retrospective awareness of past failure, but the willing spirit sought is a forward-oriented gift rather than a memory-function.

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The corpus is largely silent on humility's relationship to the memory faculty. The implicit evidence (T3.3.1) suggests that humility may *preserve* the moral-memory function by keeping the person genuinely receptive to learning from the past, while pride distorts or suppresses it. But this is analytical inference from the pattern, not direct evidence from the meaning corpus. The finding is: humility appears to enable the kind of moral memory that the ka.na narrative pattern implies is necessary for sustained covenant faithfulness, but the evidence does not directly evidence this connexion.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The corpus does not directly evidence submission's effect on the memory faculty as enabling, deepening, bypassing, or impairing it. The memory-function appears as a background supporting role (tracking consistency, informing trust-assessments) rather than as a direct faculty the characteristic acts upon. The absence of direct evidence is noted.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct relationship between contrition and the memory faculty. Analytically, genuine contrition likely involves remembering one's failure accurately, but this is inferred beyond the two-verse evidence.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct relationship between meekness/gentleness and the memory faculty.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct relationship between semnotēs and the memory faculty.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct relationship between willing-heartedness and the memory faculty.

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The near-silence on memory reveals that memory is not a primary constitutional faculty engaged by humility. The characteristic is primarily volitional, relational, and dispositional; its relationship to the memory function is indirect. The corpus would require expansion (or cross-reference to CHAR-3 contrition, which is more explicitly tied to the moral memory of specific failures) to evidence this dimension more directly.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The near-silence on memory reveals that memory is not a primary constitutional faculty in the submission characteristic's operation. The characteristic's primary faculties are will, heart, conscience, and (in its auditory engagement) the perceptive hearing. Memory appears as a supporting function that tracks reliability and informs trust rather than as a faculty the characteristic directly engages.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The silence on memory reveals that the characteristic's primary constitutional reach is to the spirit and heart in the present moment of brokenness rather than to the memory's backward-looking function. Contrition in this corpus is constituted by the present inner state before God, not by the retrospective memory of past events.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The silence suggests that the characteristic's primary constitutional engagement is with the will, perception, and cognitive self-assessment rather than with the memory faculty's retrospective function.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The silence confirms that semnotēs operates primarily in the present-characterological and relational-social registers rather than through the memory's retrospective function.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The silence confirms that willing-heartedness operates primarily in the forward-oriented volitional-affective register (freely moving toward giving and service) rather than in the retrospective memory function.

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, significantly. The ka.na corpus repeatedly pairs humbling with weeping: 2Ki22:19 — "you have torn your clothes and wept before me"; 2Ch34:27 — "you have torn your clothes and wept before me." The weeping is the affective correlate of genuine humbling — the inner act of self-lowering produces or is accompanied by grief over one's situation before God. 2Cor12:21 names the grief Paul anticipates if God humbles him before the congregation — "I may have to mourn over many of those who sinned." Phili4:12 names the inner experience of "being brought low" — a felt state of deprivation that Paul has learned to navigate with contentment. Act20:19 names "tears" as the accompaniment of sustained humility in ministry.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes. The most direct affective engagement is in Phili2:12 — "with fear and trembling" — fear as the reverential affect accompanying genuine submission of will. Col3:22 — "fearing the Lord" — the same reverential affect as the motivational ground. 2Cor7:15 — "with fear and trembling" as the affective expression of the Corinthians' obedient reception of Titus. 1Pe1:22 — obedience to truth producing "sincere brotherly love from a pure heart" — love is the affective fruit produced in the person by sustained submission to truth. Affective engagement is both at the origin of the submission (reverential fear as motivator) and at its fruit (love as product).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, as its primary constitutional dimension (T1.8.1). Psa34:18 — "brokenhearted" — the heart's breaking is an acute affective event; the brokenness of the heart is fundamentally an emotional-experiential state. Isa57:15 — "contrite spirit" — the spirit's crushed state is an affectively-loaded condition. The characteristic is constitutively affective: it is an inner suffering, a genuine grief over one's condition before God, not merely a cognitive self-assessment.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes, and this is the most analytically interesting dimension of metriopatheō. The term compound (metrios + patheō) names a *measured experience of passion/feeling* — affective engagement within measure. Heb5:2 — "he can deal gently with the ignorant and wayward, since he himself is beset with weakness" — the shared-weakness ground is affectively resonant: the high priest feels something of the erring person's condition through his own experience of limitation. The characteristic is affectively engaged (feeling with/compassion) but in a calibrated form — not feeling so much that objectivity is lost, nor so little that coldness replaces compassion. Metriopatheō is thus the measure-of-affect characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs engages the affective faculty in the sense that the settled gravity it names has an affective tone: sober, weighty seriousness (1Ti2:2 — "sober, weighty seriousness of character") is not emotionally cold but carries the settled, composed affective quality of genuine inner gravitas. The characteristic excludes both excessive emotional display and cold affective detachment — it is the composed, settled affective tone of genuine moral gravity. 1Ti3:4 — the orderly compliance produced in children by the overseer's dignity implies an affective response of appropriate regard that the dignity evokes.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes, as part of the primary volitional-affective dimension (T1.8.1). Psa51:12 — "restore to me the joy of your salvation, and uphold me with a willing spirit" — the willing spirit is paired directly with the joy of salvation; the characteristic has an affective dimension of gladness and joy. The freely-moved heart of VCG-01 (Exo35:5/22; 2Ch29:31) carries an implicit affective quality: the "spontaneous, internally-motivated generosity" (2Ch29:31 Pass A meaning) is not affectively neutral but joyfully motivated. The characteristic is the will and the joy together — the gladly-willing rather than the grimly-compliant.

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *enables and deepens* genuine affect, specifically grief and tenderness as responses to genuine reality. 2Ch34:27 ("your heart was tender") pairs heart-tenderness with humbling: the humble heart is a tender heart — capable of genuine feeling rather than defended against it. The Colossian material evidences the converse: the self-enclosed ascetic (Col2:18) is "puffed up" — a state of inflated self-satisfaction that precludes genuine grief, tenderness, and the affective dimension of authentic humility. Genuine humility enables the affective faculty to respond to what is genuinely real (one's own failing, God's word, others' need) rather than to defend against it. The cultivated contentment of Phili4:12 also evidences an affective stability produced by sustained navigation of lowliness — not the absence of affect but its ordered stability.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *enables and produces* genuine affect. 1Pe1:22 evidences that sustained obedience to truth produces "sincere brotherly love from a pure heart" — the characteristic produces a deep, genuine affective capacity that does not exist apart from the inner formation of submission. The fear-and-trembling affect (Phili2:12; 2Cor7:15) is not an impairment of affect but its rightly-ordered expression — reverential awe as the appropriate affective response to the authority being submitted to. Submission enables affect to be genuine (from a pure heart) rather than performed (eye-service, which is affect-bypassing — Col3:22).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *enables and expresses* genuine affect — specifically the affective response of grief and brokenness that accurately corresponds to the moral reality. The characteristic is not an impairment of affect but its most genuine expression at the point of moral failure before God. By opening toward God's reviving (Isa57:15), contrition also enables the subsequent positive affect of restoration and new vitality — the revived spirit and heart carry a positive affective tone that follows from the characteristic's resolution through God's response.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Metriopatheō *enables and calibrates* genuine affect. The "measured" quality does not suppress affect but holds it within appropriate measure — the characteristic enables compassionate feeling without excessive affect that distorts judgment. The structural absence of metriopatheō produces either cold affective detachment (no feeling) or unregulated affect (excessive feeling that impairs calibrated response). The characteristic enables the affective faculty to function as compassion without being overwhelmed.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *orders and composes* the affective dimension — it is the character quality that prevents both emotional volatility (which would undermine dignity) and affective coldness (which would make it merely formal gravity). The "sober" quality of semnotēs (1Ti2:2 — "sober, weighty seriousness") engages the affective faculty in its composed, ordered form.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *enables and expresses* genuine joyful affect. Psa51:12 — "restore the joy of your salvation" immediately preceding "uphold me with a willing spirit" — positions the willing spirit as the condition for joyful devotion; the characteristic enables genuine joyful affective engagement rather than affectively flat compliance. The freely-moved generous heart (Exo35:5/22) implies an affective tone of gladness in giving — the characteristic enables the affective faculty to experience giving as joyful rather than burdensome.

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The pattern reveals that humility is not a cold cognitive-volitional posture but one that engages and enables genuine feeling. The consistent pairing of genuine humbling with weeping and heart-tenderness (2Ki22:19; 2Ch34:27; Act20:19 — tears) suggests that authentic humility is *affectively warm* — it opens the person to genuine emotional response to their situation before God. This is analytically significant in distinguishing genuine humility from the performed asceticism of Col2 (which has the appearance of wisdom but is affectively cold — self-referential and pride-driven beneath the surface). The affective engagement of weeping and tenderness is a marker of genuine humility as against its counterfeit.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The pattern reveals that submission is not an emotionally cold or affect-bypassing characteristic. Its affective register is primarily reverential (fear-and-trembling) at the initiating end and love (pure heart, sincere brotherly love) at the formed end — with the reverential affect motivating the genuine submission and the love-affect being its long-term fruit. The characteristic requires and produces genuine affect rather than suppressing it.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that contrition is the characteristic most directly constituted by an affective state — the broken heart and crushed spirit are affective realities, not merely cognitive positions. This distinguishes contrition from humility (CHAR-1 — primarily dispositional-volitional) and submission (CHAR-2 — primarily volitional-relational): contrition is the most affectively loaded of the three characteristics, the one where the inner suffering is constitutive rather than incidental to the characteristic's existence.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that metriopatheō is the characteristic most directly named in relation to the calibration of affect — the measured passion-within-appropriate-measure. This distinguishes the characteristic from pure volitional strength (which might act without feeling) and from pure emotional response (which might feel without calibration). The characteristic is the integrating quality of feeling-within-appropriate-measure that enables both compassionate engagement and measured response.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that semnotēs is not an emotionally flat characteristic but one with a specific affective tone: composed, settled seriousness. The characteristic neither suppresses genuine feeling nor allows unordered emotional display — it is the character quality that holds the affective faculty in the ordered composure appropriate to the person's role and context.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that willing-heartedness and joy are structurally connected inner-being qualities: the willing spirit (Psa51:12) is associated with the joy of salvation; the generous/willing heart (Exo35; 2Ch29:31) is the inner condition of spontaneous, gladly-motivated giving. This connection is the ground of the carry-forward cross-register flag with M04 (Joy/Delight) — the two characteristics operate in adjacent affective territory where willing generosity and joyful delight naturally co-occur.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The Humility corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the creative faculty (imagination, originative capacity). The characteristic's primary engagements are relational, volitional, cognitive, and affective. There is no verse in the evidence that connects humility to creative or imaginative function.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The Submission corpus does not directly evidence engagement with the creative faculty (imagination, originative capacity). The characteristic's primary constitutional engagements are volitional, relational, and cognitive. No verse in §3.A connects submission to creative or imaginative function.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. The characteristic's constitutional reach is to spirit and heart in a state of acute brokenness, not to the creative-imaginative faculty.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. The characteristic's constitutional reach is to will, perception, cognition, and affect in the quality-of-engagement register rather than to creative or imaginative function.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. Semnotēs operates in the ordering and authenticating register rather than the creative-imaginative register.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

1Ch28:21 evidences a connexion: "every willing man who has skill for any kind of service" — the "any kind of service" implies creative/skilled engagement; the temple craftsmen's willing-hearted participation in building enabled the creative deployment of diverse crafts. The characteristic enables creative skilled service rather than suppressing it. However, the creative faculty is not the primary constitutional engagement — willingness is what enables the creative skill to be deployed, rather than the characteristic being constitutively creative itself.

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct connexion between humility and creative or imaginative capacity. Analytically, one might infer that the epistemic-virtue function of humility (enabling accurate perception and cognition — see T3.1.2 and T3.2.2) might indirectly free the creative faculty from self-referential constraints, but this is inference beyond the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The evidence is silent on any direct connexion between submission and creative or imaginative capacity. The characteristic operates in the authority-relationship register rather than the creative-generative register.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on any relationship between contrition and creative or imaginative capacity.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on any relationship between meekness/gentleness and creative or imaginative capacity.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The evidence is silent on any relationship between semnotēs and creative or imaginative capacity.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *enables* creative faculty deployment. 1Ch28:21 — "willing man who has skill for any kind of service" — the pairing of willingness with skill-across-all-kinds implies that the willing person brings their full creative and skilled repertoire to the service. The characteristic enables rather than constrains the creative faculty by removing the reluctance-friction that would limit creative engagement to the minimum required.

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The silence on creative faculty engagement reveals that humility's constitutional reach is primarily interpersonal and relational (between person, God, and others) rather than creative or generative. The characteristic opens the person toward genuine relation and accurate self-knowledge; it does not evidence itself in the creative-imaginative register.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The silence on creative faculty engagement reveals that submission's constitutional reach is constitutively relational-responsive (oriented toward authorities and commands) rather than originating-creative. The characteristic is structured by reception-and-yielding rather than origination-and-generation.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The silence confirms that contrition's constitutional focus is narrowly on the person's inner moral-relational state before God rather than on creative or generative capacities.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The silence confirms the characteristic operates in the quality-of-engagement-with-others register rather than the creative-generative register.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The silence confirms semnotēs operates in the character-ordering-social register rather than the creative-generative register.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The 1Ch28:21 pattern reveals that willing-heartedness is the *enabling condition for wholehearted creative skilled service* — it is not itself creative but enables creativity to be deployed fully. This is one of the most distinctive findings about CHAR-6: it enables other faculties (creativity, skill) to be fully expressed rather than partially deployed under reluctant compliance.

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Volition is the primary constitutional faculty engaged by humility. The evidence is extensive: Jam4:10 — "humble yourselves" (imperative to the volitional capacity); 1Pe5:6 — "humble yourselves therefore under the mighty hand of God" (deliberate act of self-placement); Phili2:3 — "in humility count others more significant" (volitional cognitive reordering); Phili2:8 — Christ "humbled himself" (the most extreme volitional act in the corpus — self-determination to the point of death); Col3:12 — "put on… humility" (the act of character-deliberate choice); Mat18:4 — "whoever humbles himself like this child" (reflexive volitional act). The characteristic is constitutionally a volitional act and disposition before it is anything else — the will that chooses its own downward posture.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Volition is the primary constitutional faculty. The evidence is extensive: Gal2:5 (submission as a decisive volitional act that can be withheld); Heb11:8 (Abraham obeyed — a faith-driven volitional event); Phili2:12 (sustained inner disposition of "always obeyed" — the will's ongoing orientation); 1Ti2:11 (whole-hearted receptivity — volitional openness of the learner); Rom6:16/17 (the will's habitual yielding determining whose servant one is); 2Cor10:5 (taking every thought captive — the will directing the mind). The characteristic is constitutively volitional — it is the will's act and disposition that defines whether submission is genuine.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The volitional element is present but secondary. The person who remains in genuine contrition rather than fleeing into hardening, self-justification, or despair is exercising a passive-receptive volitional openness — the will that does not resist the crushed state but remains open to it and to God's response to it. Isa57:15 — the person "of a contrite and lowly spirit" — the characterological form suggests a sustained volitional posture of remaining in the crushed state rather than recovering into self-sufficiency.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes, as the primary faculty (T1.8.1). Metriopatheō (Heb5:2) — "can deal gently" — names a volitional capacity: the will that chooses and maintains measured engagement rather than defaulting to severity or detachment. Okneō (Act9:38) — the volitional readiness that moves without hesitation — names the will's kinetic quality directly. Both terms are fundamentally volitional in their constitution.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes, as a secondary enabling dimension. Tit2:7 — "show integrity, dignity" — the showing implies a volitional choice to inhabit and express the character quality; the characteristic must be maintained through volitional commitment to the manner it requires. 1Ti3:4 — "with all dignity" — the comprehensive adverb implies a sustained volitional commitment to the characteristic's expression across all household management situations.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Volition is the primary faculty, as established in T1.8.1. All five verses evidence the volitional dimension: the will's free movement (Exo35:5/22 — willing heart), the will's person-defining orientation (1Ch28:21 — every willing man), the will's contextual expression (2Ch29:31 — willing heart in worship), and the will's spirit-level quality requiring divine sustaining (Psa51:12 — willing spirit). The characteristic is constitutively volitional — it is the quality and direction of the will (free, uncoerced, gladly-oriented) that defines it.

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility both *requires* volition and *rightly orders* it. The imperative form throughout ("humble yourselves") presupposes and addresses the volitional capacity. The Phili2:8 paradigm reveals that the volitional act of self-humbling is the highest exercise of free self-determination — choosing, from a position of full capability and freedom, to take the downward path. This suggests that humility does not impair volition but *expresses* it in its highest form: the will most fully itself when it freely releases the claim to standing rather than defending it. Conversely, pride (the structural opposite) represents the will enclosed in self-assertion — technically free but functionally self-limiting in its capacities for genuine relation and perception.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *rightly orders and deepens* volition. The characteristic requires the will's own active engagement — "humble yourselves," "obey," "yield" — all address the will's capacity. The submission that produces pure-heart love (1Pe1:22) and sustained conscience-grounded character (Phili2:12) shows the will operating at its deepest and most self-directed level — not suppressed but oriented under legitimate authority. Rom6:16/17 reveals the most significant volitional insight: the will's habitual yielding determines whose servant one is — meaning the will is what is most at stake in submission. Genuine submission requires the will to be most fully engaged, not bypassed.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *rightly orders* the will by stripping the self-asserting, self-protective volitional orientation that prevents genuine openness to God. The crushed spirit (Psa34:18) is one whose will no longer asserts itself in proud self-sufficiency; the characteristic enables the will to be genuinely receptive rather than defensively closed. The reviving that follows (Isa57:15) produces a renewed volitional capacity that flows from the cleared ground of the contrite spirit.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Meekness/gentleness *rightly orders and expresses* volition. Metriopatheō enables the will to act proportionately rather than reactively — the measured quality requires the will to calibrate its response rather than defaulting to whatever impulse arises. Okneō (Act9:38) reveals the will's most freely-expressed quality: the will that does not generate inner friction or resistance when called to respond. Both aspects of the characteristic express the will at its most freely and proportionately functioning.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *orders and directs* volition toward settled, non-self-asserting expression. The characteristic provides the inner character-ground from which volitional choices about manner and comportment flow appropriately — the person of semnotēs makes choices about how they inhabit their roles from a settled inner quality rather than from anxious self-assertion. The characteristic enables volition to function from a grounded inner position rather than from insecure self-promotion.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *expresses and enables* the will at its most liberated. The freely-moved will (Exo35:5/22) is the will functioning at maximum voluntary freedom — not constrained, not compelled, but springing forward from genuine inner motivation. The characteristic enables volition to operate in its purest form: genuinely self-determined rather than externally-determined. Psa51:12 confirms the inverse: without the willing spirit (after moral failure), the will cannot exercise this free movement and requires divine restoration.

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that humility is fundamentally a *choice-structured* characteristic: it cannot be imposed on the will from outside without ceasing to be genuine humility and becoming mere experienced lowliness (the M09-B condition register). The distinction between M09-A (willed self-lowering) and M09-B (imposed lowliness) maps directly onto the distinction between volitionally-engaged and volitionally-bypassed humility. The Col2:23 critique of imposed asceticism confirms this: external constraint cannot produce genuine inner transformation. Genuine humility is constitutively volitional — it requires the person's own choice — which is precisely what makes the Phili2:8 paradigm so striking: the divine Son freely *choosing* the downward path.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that submission is the characteristic most directly constituted by the will. Without volitional engagement, what remains is mere compliance (the M09-C/D distinction is precisely this: M09-C carries the genuine will-submission face; M09-D carries the relational-pattern expression). The volitional character of submission makes it the characteristic in which the will's orientation is most transparently at issue — whose servant the person is, and at what depth they genuinely yield, is determined by the will's habitual orientation (Rom6:16/17). The will is not merely the instrument of submission; it is the constitutional site where submission is determined.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that contrition operates on the will by dissolving its proud self-assertion — the will is not suppressed but reoriented from defensive self-protection to open receptivity. This makes contrition the characteristic that clears the ground for renewed volitional orientation — the revived spirit and heart (Isa57:15) imply a renewed volitional capacity that follows from the characteristic's resolution through God's presence.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that meekness and gentleness are expressions of *free, non-reactive willing*. The will that is meek/gentle is one that has freedom from two kinds of compulsion: (a) the compulsion to react with severity (metriopatheō restrains this) and (b) the compulsion to hesitate with self-protective reluctance (okneō absence restrains this). The characteristic is the will in its most liberated form — free from reactive extremes in both directions.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that semnotēs is maintained through sustained volitional commitment but is not constitutively an act of will — it is a character quality that persists and from which volitional choices flow. The distinction is that volition is secondary (maintains and expresses the characteristic) while the characterological quality is primary (the upstream source from which volitional expression flows).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that willing-heartedness is the *positive pole of the volitional faculty* — the will in its most freely-expressed, most genuinely-self-determined form. It is not the will suppressed (coerced compliance) nor the will in neutral (neither willing nor unwilling) but the will actively and gladly moving toward good. This makes the characteristic the expression of volitional health and freedom rather than of volitional constraint.

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Agency is engaged, but in a distinctive directional form: humility exercises agency *downward* rather than upward. The ka.na corpus evidences the person *initiating* the act of humbling — Josiah humbling himself when he hears the word (2Ch34:27), Manasseh initiating entreaty in distress (2Ch33:12), Hezekiah humbling in response to identified pride (2Ch32:26). These are genuine acts of inner agency — the person does something. Paul's self-lowering in 2Cor11:7 is an agentive choice ("I humbled myself so that you might be exalted"). Phili2:8 — Christ "humbled himself by becoming obedient to the point of death" — the agentic form is striking: Christ is the *subject* who acts downward. Agency in humility is real agency but it is agency in the direction of self-lowering rather than self-assertion or self-elevation.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Agency is engaged, but specifically directed toward yielding to rather than initiating from. Heb11:8 — Abraham "obeyed when he was called" — his agency is exercised in the act of going, but the initiative was the divine call; his agency is the active response to external initiative rather than self-originated action. Act6:7 — the priests "became obedient to the faith" — their agency exercised in the decisive act of reorientation. 2Cor9:13 — the generous giving that flows from submission to the gospel — agency in action directed by the submission of the will. Agency in submission is real but specifically *responsive* rather than self-originated: the person exercises genuine agency in yielding and in the actions that flow from yielding.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence engagement of the agency faculty by contrition. The characteristic is evidenced as a state the person is in rather than a capacity to act. The agency dimension is primarily on God's side in this corpus: God is the one who draws near, saves, dwells, and revives.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes, particularly through okneō (Act9:38). The disciples urge Peter to come "without delay" — the expected quality is the agency that moves immediately and without hesitation. The characteristic expressed through okneō absence is precisely the *prompt, unimpeded exercise of agency* in response to genuine need. Metriopatheō also involves agency: the high priest actively deals gently with the erring — the gentle dealing is an agentive act, not a passive state.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes. 1Ti3:4 — the overseer managing his household "with all dignity" — the agency of household management is exercised through and with the characteristic: the managing is the agentive act; the dignity is the quality with which it is exercised. Tit2:7 — "show integrity, dignity" — the showing is an agentive act that carries the characteristic. Agency is the vehicle through which semnotēs is expressed.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes. The freely-moved heart immediately produces the agentive act of bringing: Exo35:5 — "let him bring"; Exo35:22 — "brought brooches and earrings"; 2Ch29:31 — "brought burnt offerings." The willing heart directly enables and produces the agentive act. 1Ch28:21 — "every willing man… will be wholly at your command" — the willing person's agency is fully available for service. Agency in this characteristic is maximally expressed: the willing-hearted person acts fully and freely.

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *rightly orders and deepens* agency. Jam4:6 — "God gives grace to the humble" — suggests that the humble person receives divine enabling that the proud person does not; this implies that the humble person's capacity to act effectively is enhanced rather than diminished by the posture of self-lowering. The exaltation-pattern (Mat18:4; Mat23:12; 1Pe5:6 — the humble will be exalted "at the proper time") suggests that voluntary self-lowering is ultimately followed by God's own agentive reversal in the person's favour. Humility does not permanently diminish agency but redirects it — away from self-assertion and toward genuine service of others (2Cor11:7; Act20:19) and God (Phili2:8).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *rightly directs and sustains* agency. Phile21 — Paul's confidence in Philemon's obedience anticipating action "beyond what I say" — genuine submission produces agency that exceeds the minimum commanded; submission unleashes agency rather than containing it. 1Pe1:22 — "love one another earnestly from a pure heart" — the agency of earnest love flows from the soul-purification produced by submission. The characteristic does not impair agency but redirects it from self-serving to other-serving and authority-responsive directions.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *clears the ground for renewed agency*. Isa57:15 — "revive the spirit of the lowly, and to revive the heart of the contrite" — the reviving that God's response produces implies a restored inner vitality that would enable renewed agency. The crushed state (Psa34:18) may temporarily suspend the person's agentic self-projection; God's reviving (Isa57:15) enables its renewed operation from a ground no longer distorted by proud self-assertion.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Meekness/gentleness *enables and frees* agency. Okneō (Act9:38) — the absence of hesitation enables agency to function at its most immediately responsive. The person who lacks okneō generates internal friction that delays or prevents responsive agency. Metriopatheō (Heb5:2) enables the high priest to exercise his mediating agency appropriately — without the characteristic, his agency might be deployed in severity (excessive) or detachment (absent). The characteristic calibrates and liberates agency in its appropriate expression.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *enables ordered and credible agency*. The overseer's dignity enables his household management to be effective (1Ti3:4 — producing orderly compliance) rather than requiring coercive force. Tit2:7 — dignity authenticating teaching enables the agentive act of instruction to be received as genuine. The characteristic enables agency to produce the effects it seeks (order, compliance, reception of instruction) through the quality of the manner rather than through force or performance.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *maximally enables agency*. 1Ch28:21 — the willing craftsmen place their full agency at the service of the temple work; 2Ch29:31 — beyond-required burnt offerings express maximally voluntary agency (more than required). The characteristic enables agency to exceed minimums — the willing person does not merely comply but freely gives beyond what is required, which is the fullest expression of human agency. Psa51:12 confirms the inverse: without the willing spirit, sustained devotional agency is not possible — the person cannot freely give what they are burdened from giving.

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that humility is an *active* rather than passive characteristic. The M09-B evidence (experienced lowliness — Phili4:12; 2Cor7:6) shows the passive register, but even there, what is commended is the cultivated active response of contentment (Phili4:12 — "I have learned the secret"). Humility is not the suppression of agency but its reorientation: the will acts, but it acts toward God and others rather than toward its own elevation. This distinguishes humility from quietism (the passive suppression of will and agency) and from servility (agency-absence from external pressure).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that submission is not a passive characteristic. The will actively yields; the person actively receives the authority's claim and actively orients toward it. Phile21 (going beyond the minimum) and 1Pe1:22 (earnest love from a pure heart) confirm that genuine submission produces rather than suppresses genuine agency. The characteristic is the inner posture that rightly orients agency rather than eliminating it.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The pattern reveals that contrition operates as a suspension and renewal of agency rather than a permanent impairment: the crushed spirit's self-asserting agency is suspended, and God's reviving restores a cleaner form of inner vitality and capacity. The characteristic is thus a transitional state for agency — passing through rather than ending in.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that meekness and gentleness are agency-enabling rather than agency-suppressing: the meek/gentle person is not a passive non-actor but one whose agency is appropriately calibrated and immediately responsive. The characteristic enables the full and appropriate exercise of agency without the distortions of reactive severity or self-protective hesitation.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The pattern reveals that semnotēs is an *agency-enabling character quality* — it provides the inner ground from which effective, credible agentive action flows. Leadership and teaching agency without semnotēs may technically occur but lacks the character-grounded effectiveness that the characteristic enables. The characteristic is thus the inner enabling condition for the agency of leadership and instruction to be genuinely effective.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The pattern reveals that willing-heartedness is an *agency-maximising quality* — where it is present, the person gives more than required (2Ch29:31 — beyond-required offerings), serves fully (1Ch28:21 — wholly at command), and acts immediately without friction (Exo35:22 — brought). The characteristic is what enables human agency to reach its fullest expression in giving and service, and its absence (Psa51:12 — requiring restoration) is what limits that expression.

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, and foundationally. The entire ka.na corpus evidences humility as a response to moral evaluation: the person humbles themselves after recognising their moral failure, guilt, or the righteousness of God's judgment. 2Ch12:6 — "the princes and king humbled themselves and said, 'The Lord is righteous'" — the moral evaluation of God as right and their own position as requiring acknowledgment is the immediate precipitant of the humbling. Lev26:41 — the "uncircumcised heart humbled" — the inner turning from hardness involves a moral evaluation of one's own condition. 2Ch32:26 — Hezekiah humbles himself "for the pride of his heart" — the internal moral evaluation of his own pride produces the humbling. Humility requires genuine moral evaluation as its cognitive-evaluative precondition.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, centrally. Eph6:1 — "obey your parents in the Lord, for this is right" — moral rightness is the explicit ground of the obedience command; the moral evaluation faculty assesses the authority as legitimate and the submission as right. Gal2:5 — Paul's non-submission to false teachers is a principled moral evaluation of their illegitimacy; the decision to withhold submission requires evaluating the authority's legitimacy against the gospel. Pro30:17 — disobedience to a mother as "fatal moral failure" — moral evaluation is the interpretive frame. Col3:22 — "fearing the Lord" as the moral-theological ground of genuine submission — the fear of God is a moral evaluation of God as the ultimate authority. The moral evaluation faculty provides both the legitimacy-assessment and the motivation for the characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, as its necessary precondition. Genuine contrition requires genuine moral evaluation — an accurate assessment of one's own failure before God's standard of right and holy. Without the moral evaluation faculty functioning genuinely (perceiving the moral reality of one's failure rather than distorting it through self-justification), the characteristic cannot be genuine. Isa57:15's pairing of contrition with the high-and-holy God implies that the moral evaluation that occasions contrition is an assessment made in the light of divine holiness — the most demanding and accurate standard.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes. Metriopatheō (Heb5:2) requires moral evaluation in two directions: (a) the evaluation of the erring person's condition as "ignorant and wayward" — a moral assessment that determines the appropriate form of engagement; and (b) the evaluation of one's own condition as "beset with weakness" — the moral self-assessment that enables the gentleness rather than severity. The "measured" quality of metriopatheō requires ongoing moral calibration: assessing what measure of engagement is appropriate to the situation.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes. Tit2:7 — dignity alongside integrity — integrity (aphthorian — incorruptibility, soundness) names the moral character dimension; semnotēs is paired with it as a companion quality. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged in the consistent self-assessment required to maintain dignity in all contexts (1Ti2:2 — "in every way"; 1Ti3:4 — "with all dignity") — the person must evaluate what constitutes appropriate seriousness in each social context and maintain it.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The moral evaluation faculty is engaged in assessing the invitation to give and the appropriateness of the response. Exo35:5 — "take from among you a contribution to the Lord" — the willing-hearted person morally evaluates the call as genuine and appropriate, and their inner orientation responds accordingly. 2Ch29:31 — the context of restored worship and offering implies the moral evaluation that bringing offerings is right and good. Psa51:12's penitential context involves the moral evaluation of one's own failure (Psa51:1–11 — the extended moral self-evaluation that precedes the prayer for a willing spirit).

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *enables and deepens* moral evaluation. Pro11:2 — "with the humble is wisdom" — and the evidence that the humble person can identify their own fault (Hezekiah in 2Ch32:26; Josiah in 2Ch34:27) suggest that the humble person's moral evaluation faculty operates without the distortion that pride introduces. Col2:18 identifies the "sensuous mind" operating beneath false humility as a site of distorted moral evaluation — the puffed-up person cannot accurately evaluate their own moral condition. Genuine humility enables accurate moral self-assessment because it does not require the protective distortions that maintain the illusion of rightness.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Submission *enables and deepens* moral evaluation. Rom16:19 — Paul redirects the Romans' obedient disposition toward "wisdom as to what is good and innocence as to what is evil" — the obedient will is the posture from which genuine moral discernment grows. Gal2:5 — the willingness to withhold submission when the authority is illegitimate evidences that genuine submission presupposes and deepens moral evaluation (the person must be able to assess the authority's legitimacy). The submission that bypasses moral evaluation — yielding without assessing the authority's legitimacy — is the Milgram-style pathological compliance that the evidence (Gal2:5 as principled non-submission) specifically guards against.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Contrition *presupposes and validates* moral evaluation. The person who arrives at genuine contrition has allowed their moral evaluation faculty to function without self-protective distortion — the breaking is, in part, the event of genuine moral self-knowledge before God's holiness. The characteristic confirms and deepens accurate moral evaluation by its very existence: the crushed spirit is evidence that the moral evaluation faculty has genuinely perceived the person's condition rather than protecting the self from that perception.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Meekness/gentleness *deepens and calibrates* moral evaluation. The shared-weakness self-awareness (Heb5:2) that grounds metriopatheō prevents the moral evaluation faculty from operating with prideful distortion — the person who genuinely knows their own weakness assesses others' moral conditions more accurately. The characteristic enables the moral evaluation faculty to function without the distortion of assumed superiority that harshness introduces.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs *enables and confirms* genuine moral evaluation in the sense that the person of genuine semnotēs is one whose moral seriousness is authentic rather than performed. Tit2:7 — teaching that has both integrity and dignity is teaching whose moral evaluation is genuine — the integrity is the moral content; the dignity is the character-gravity that confirms the moral content is genuinely held rather than performed. The characteristic thus confirms that the moral evaluation faculty is functioning genuinely rather than performing its function for display.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Willing-heartedness *enables genuine moral evaluation* to produce the appropriate response. The person whose inner will is freely-oriented toward God can respond genuinely to the moral evaluation's conclusion (giving is right and good) — the evaluation and the will's response are aligned. The person without willing-heartedness may evaluate giving as right but find their will unresponsive to the moral evaluation's conclusion — the moral evaluation faculty functions but the will does not follow.

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The pattern reveals that humility is both *enabled by* and *enabling of* accurate moral evaluation. It is a bidirectional relationship: genuine moral evaluation of one's situation before God occasions the inner act of humbling (the ka.na pattern); and the posture of humility, once established, deepens the capacity for continued accurate moral assessment (Pro11:2 — wisdom follows humility). This bidirectionality makes humility a foundational virtue in the moral sense: it is not only a single virtue but a condition for the accurate functioning of the moral evaluation faculty across the person's whole inner life.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The pattern reveals that genuine submission in the biblical corpus is always morally evaluated: the authority's legitimacy is assessed (Gal2:5 — withholding from false teachers; Eph6:1 — "in the Lord, for this is right"). This is the primary point where the biblical corpus diverges from social-psychological compliance research (which documents compliance without moral evaluation). Genuine submission requires moral evaluation as a constituent — the person submits because they have assessed that the authority is legitimate and the submission is right. This makes submission an expression of moral wisdom rather than a suspension of it.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The pattern reveals that contrition is the affective-existential consequence of genuine moral evaluation before divine holiness — it is what the moral evaluation faculty's accurate functioning feels like when it genuinely confronts the person's moral condition. The characteristic thus stands as evidence that the moral evaluation faculty is operating honestly rather than in self-protective distortion.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The pattern reveals that metriopatheō (Heb5:2) requires the moral evaluation faculty to be applied to oneself before it is applied to others — the self-assessment of shared weakness (Heb5:2) precedes and enables the calibrated assessment of the erring other's condition. The characteristic thus produces a *self-other moral evaluation sequence* that prevents the double-standard of harsh judgment toward others without acknowledgment of one's own limitation.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The pattern reveals that semnotēs and integrity (Tit2:7) together constitute the full character-authenticity of genuine moral agency: integrity is the moral-evaluative content (what is right and true); dignity is the settled gravity with which that content is held and expressed. The characteristic is thus the *character-quality that authenticates moral evaluation* — it confirms that the moral seriousness expressed is genuine inner conviction rather than performed gravitas.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The pattern reveals that willing-heartedness is the *volitional bridge between moral evaluation and action* — it is what enables the will to follow the moral evaluation's conclusion rather than remaining in the gap between knowing-good and doing-good. The freely-moved will is the faculty that enables the moral evaluation's conclusion to become actual conduct without the friction of reluctance.

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Conscience engagement is clearly present. Lev26:41 — the "uncircumcised heart" that must be humbled is a conscience-adjacent term: the uncircumcised heart is the inner faculty that has not been penetrated by the moral reality of one's situation; humbling involves that penetration. The ka.na corpus evidences humbling consistently following divine address that awakens the conscience: 2Ki22:19 (hearing God's words against the place and its inhabitants — the conscience registers the personal claim of universal judgment); 2Ch33:12 (Manasseh in distress — acute awareness of his sin's consequences); 2Ch33:23 (Amon's increasing guilt as the correlate of not humbling — conscience function impaired by persistent non-humbling). Conscience in this corpus functions as the inner witness that sin and failure are genuinely one's own and require a response.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, explicitly and distinctively. Phili2:12 — sustained obedience rooted in "fear of God rather than social pressure" — the conscience functions as the internal sustainer when external accountability is removed. The conscience provides the inner verdict that the submission is right and maintains it without external reinforcement. Col3:22 — "fearing the Lord" — the theological-moral orientation of the conscience toward God's authority. Eph6:1 — "for this is right" — the conscience's verdict of moral rightness as the ground of the obedience command.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, directly. Contrition is the acute inner state that a functioning conscience produces when it genuinely registers the moral weight of the person's failure before God. The brokenhearted and crushed in spirit (Psa34:18) are those whose conscience has genuinely registered the gravity of their condition — the breaking is the conscience's accurate witness becoming felt reality rather than merely acknowledged proposition. Isa57:15 — the contrite in spirit as those whom God revives — confirms that the contrite state is the fruit of a genuinely functioning conscience rather than its distortion.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The conscience is engaged through the self-assessment of shared weakness (Heb5:2). Genuine conscience function — the inner witness of one's own moral condition — is what enables the high priest to know that "he himself is beset with weakness." This self-knowledge through conscience function is the enabling ground of metriopatheō. The person whose conscience is suppressed or non-functioning cannot access the self-awareness of shared weakness that enables gentleness.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs engages the conscience through its pairing with integrity (Tit2:7) — integrity names the moral-incorruptibility that genuine conscience function produces. The person of genuine semnotēs is one whose settled moral gravity is consistent with genuine conscience function — the dignity is not a social mask over a privately-compromised conscience but the outward expression of genuine inner moral seriousness. 1Ti3:4's "all dignity" implies a comprehensiveness that would not be possible with an internally-compromised conscience.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Psa51:12 directly evidences conscience-engagement. The psalm is the archetypal conscience-awakened penitential prayer — Psa51:1–11 is the extended conscience-response to David's moral failure. The request for a willing spirit (Psa51:12) comes after the conscience has fully registered the failure and its consequences. The characteristic in its VCG-02 register is thus post-conscience: it is what is sought after the conscience has done its full work of conviction and the person is ready for the spirit's renewal.

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Humility *enables and deepens* conscience function, and its absence *impairs* it. 2Ch33:23 evidences this directly: Amon's refusal to humble himself is linked to increasing guilt — the conscience registers the guilt but is not responded to, leading to accumulation. The humble person (Josiah in 2Ch34:27 — tender heart, weeping) is the person whose conscience is functioning in its full receptivity and response. By contrast, 2Ch36:12 (Zedekiah refusing to humble before the prophet) evidences conscience that has been hardened: the inner witness is present (God speaks through the prophet) but the person refuses the humbling that conscience functioning would produce. Humility enables conscience by removing the defensive self-enclosure that suppresses the inner witness.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)
