## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

*Re-reading §3.E fresh for T4's lens.*

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, in two distinct forms. First, God *humbles as a judicial and formative act*: 2Ch28:19 — "the Lord humbled Judah because of Ahaz"; Psa107:12 — "he bowed their hearts down with hard labor." God is the active agent producing the lowliness condition in the person (M09-B imposed register). Second, God responds to the human's humbling with mercy, reversal, and divine exaltation: 1Ki21:29 — God delays judgment in response to Ahab's humbling; 2Ch12:7 — God withdraws destruction; 2Ch34:27 — God confirms he has heard; Luk1:48 — God looks upon Mary's humble estate and lifts her; Luk1:52 — God exalts those of humble estate. God both produces lowliness (imposed register) and responds to the human's humbling with upward reversal. Both are operations of the characteristic from God toward the human.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, in two distinct forms. First, God *produces* the characteristic in persons through the Spirit: 1Pe1:2 — "in the sanctification of the Spirit, for obedience to Jesus Christ" — the Spirit's sanctifying work is directed toward producing the inner posture of submission in believers; God's operation is the generative source of the characteristic from the divine side. Second, God *exemplifies* the characteristic in the Son: Heb5:8 — Christ "learned obedience through what he suffered" — God in the Son takes on the human experience of submission to the Father, which becomes the paradigm for the human believer. Third, the gospel as God's word creates the occasion and demand for the obedience of faith (Rom1:5; 16:26) — God's revelatory action occasions the human response of submission.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Yes, and this is the most extensively evidenced dimension of the characteristic's relational operation. God's operation toward the contrite person is named in both verses. Psa34:18 — "the Lord is near to the brokenhearted and saves the crushed in spirit" — two divine actions: drawing near and saving. Isa57:15 — "I dwell in the high and holy place, and also with him who is of a contrite and lowly spirit, to revive the spirit of the lowly, and to revive the heart of the contrite" — two further divine actions: dwelling with and reviving. God's operation toward the contrite is thus nearness, saving, indwelling, and reviving — a comprehensive divine movement toward the person in their most broken inner state.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 evidences the characteristic operating through the Aaronic high priest as mediator from God toward the people — the high priest's metriopatheō is a priestly-mediating quality that brings God's compassionate dealing to the erring. The verse images God's disposition toward the wayward through the priest's gentle dealing. The typological dimension (T0.4.1) confirms that the divine disposition toward the erring is mediated through the gentleness of the appointed mediator — in the ultimate register, Christ's priestly sympathy (the antitype of the Aaronic high priest's metriopatheō) is the divine meekness/gentleness operating toward humanity.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Semnotēs is evidenced as a quality God requires and shapes in persons rather than as something God extends toward them directly. 1Ti2:2 pairs dignity with godliness — the dignified life is life oriented toward God; the characteristic is what godly life looks like in its manner. The requirement for semnotēs in the overseer (1Ti3:4) and in Titus (Tit2:7) are apostolic directives that reflect what God requires of those in leadership — in this sense, the standard of dignity is a divine requirement that comes through apostolic instruction. The operation is normative-formative rather than direct divine bestowal.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes, most directly in Psa51:12 — "uphold me with a willing spirit" — God is the agent who upholds (sustains, provides) the willing spirit. God operates toward the human person by sustaining and restoring the inner orientation of willing-heartedness after moral failure. In VCG-01, God's operation toward the person is less direct but present structurally: God calls for free-will offering (Exo35:5 — "a contribution to the Lord"), implying that the call itself creates the occasion for the characteristic's expression. God does not coerce the willing heart but calls for it and sustains it.

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence reveals primarily a *responsive* basis within a *covenantal* frame. The ka.na pattern is consistently: human humbling → divine response (mercy, hearing, withdrawal of judgment). 2Ch7:14 makes the covenantal conditionality explicit: "if my people… humble themselves… then I will hear from heaven and forgive." God's mercy-response to humbling is conditional on the genuine inner act, but the covenantal frame provides the structure within which the responsive basis operates. The imposed-lowering instances (2Ch28:19; Psa107:12) are not responsive in the same direction but are themselves covenantally framed — God imposes lowliness as the consequence of covenant unfaithfulness. Grace as the unconditional ground (Jam4:6 — "he gives more grace… to the humble") modifies the picture: the humble person receives grace not merely as response to achievement but because humility is the inner posture that receives what God freely gives.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The basis is *covenantal-gospel*: God's extension of the characteristic through the Spirit is framed within the covenant of grace and the gospel's proclamation. 1Pe1:2 — "according to the foreknowledge of God the Father, in the sanctification of the Spirit, for obedience to Jesus Christ" — the divine foreknowledge and elective purpose are the ground; the Spirit's sanctification is the means; obedience is the telos. The basis is thus neither unconditionally bestowed without human response (the characteristic requires the will's engagement) nor conditionally earned (it is the Spirit's work within the person). The covenantal-gospel frame holds both: God works; the person's will genuinely responds.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The basis is *responsive*: God responds to the inner state of contrition with his nearness and reviving. The evidence does not frame the divine response as conditional (if contrition, then perhaps God responds) but as direct and reliable: "the Lord is near to the brokenhearted" (Psa34:18) — the present-tense generalising statement implies a reliable characterological disposition of God toward the contrite. God's response to contrition is not arbitrary or conditional on merit but responsive to the inner state itself. Isa57:15 further frames this as characterological of God — his eternal dwelling in the high and holy place does not prevent but rather determines his dwelling with the contrite spirit.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The basis is *mediated-responsive*: God extends the characteristic through an appointed mediator (the high priest) who is equipped for gentleness precisely by sharing human weakness (Heb5:2). The basis is both responsive (God's disposition toward the erring is compassionate rather than merely judicial) and mediated (it comes through a human figure who shares the condition of those he ministers to). The grounding in shared weakness (Heb5:2) reveals that the basis of the gentleness is creaturely-empathic rather than divine-sovereign only.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The basis is *formative-normative*: God requires and shapes the characteristic through the community-formational structures of apostolic instruction (the Pastorals framework — 1Ti, Tit). The standard of semnotēs is communicated through the apostolic teaching that shapes community leadership and life. The basis is not unconditional bestowal but the formative requirement within the covenant community's ordering.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The basis is *restorative grace* (Psa51:12 — God restoring the willing spirit after failure) and *calling invitation* (Exo35:5 — God calling for free-will contribution). The basis is neither conditional-on-merit (Psa51:12's prayer is from the person in moral failure, not merit) nor merely responsive (God actively upholds and sustains the willing spirit rather than merely waiting for it). The basis is gracious-initiative: God calls for what the freely-willing person can give, and when the person has lost that capacity, God's grace restores it.

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

God's operation of humility toward humans reveals his disposition as both *corrective* and *restorative*. The imposed-lowering instances (Psa107:12 — bowing hearts down through hard labor; 2Ch28:19 — humbling Judah) are not punitive ends in themselves but corrective means: the humbling produces dependence and turns the person back toward God. Psa107:12 evidences this most acutely — "they fell down with none to help" — the experience of complete dependence is the created condition for turning to God. The responsive-mercy instances (2Ch12:7; 1Ki21:29; Luk18:14) reveal God's disposition as genuinely receptive to the inner posture of humbling — he does not remain opposed when the posture shifts. Jam4:6 ("gives more grace to the humble") reveals God's disposition as actively generous toward the humble: not merely neutral but positively oriented toward the person who takes the lowly posture.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

God's extension of submission-capacity through the Spirit (1Pe1:2) reveals his disposition as actively formative: God does not merely command submission but works to produce it in the person from within. The fact that God requires obedience of faith (Rom1:5; 16:26) as the telos of gospel proclamation reveals that God seeks the person's genuine inner yielding, not merely their outward compliance — he values the will's genuine orientation toward him. Heb5:8 (the Son learning obedience through suffering) reveals God's willingness to enter the creaturely experience of submission to form the paradigm from within — God's disposition is one of solidarity in the formation of the characteristic he requires.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

God's response reveals his disposition as one of *active movement toward the broken* rather than requiring the broken person to somehow restore themselves before approaching him. Both verses show God as the initiating party in drawing near (Psa34:18 — "the Lord is near") and dwelling with (Isa57:15 — "I dwell with him"). The divine disposition evidenced is that of one who is attracted toward the contrite and broken inner state rather than repelled by it — a disposition that inverts the ordinary human assumption that strength and achievement attract attention while weakness and brokenness are avoided.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2's high priestly metriopatheō images God's disposition as one of measured compassionate restraint toward the "ignorant and wayward" rather than immediate severe judgment. The priestly mediation as a divinely-instituted structure reveals that God has built into his covenantal order a mechanism for gentle engagement with erring humanity — the institution of priesthood is itself a disclosure of the divine disposition of measured compassionate dealing with the wayward.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The requirement for semnotēs in leadership (1Ti3:4; Tit2:7) and in the community's manner of life (1Ti2:2) reveals God's disposition as one who values settled, non-self-assertive moral gravity in those who represent him and his community. God does not value anxious self-promotion or social performance as the mark of his people and leaders — the requirement for semnotēs reveals a divine valuation of grounded, authentic inner gravity over performance and display.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

God's operation reveals a disposition of valuing genuine, uncoerced giving over compelled compliance (Exo35:5 — he calls for willing-hearted contribution rather than mandating uniform levies), and of actively restoring the inner capacity for free-giving when it is lost (Psa51:12 — upholding the willing spirit after failure). God's disposition is thus oriented toward genuine freely-given devotion — he desires the person's inner willing orientation, not merely external compliance — and he is active in sustaining that orientation beyond what the person can maintain alone.

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation is extensively evidenced (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation is evidenced (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation is the dominant dimension of the characteristic's relational evidence (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The evidence evidences God-to-human operation through the mediating high priest (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3). The operation is mediated rather than direct, but present.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The evidence addresses God's formative-normative operation (requiring and shaping the characteristic through apostolic instruction) rather than direct bestowal (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation is evidenced in both Psa51:12 (direct restoration) and Exo35:5 (inviting call) (see T4.1.1–T4.1.3).

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes; the human-toward-God direction is the dominant register of the M09-A voluntary corpus. 2Ch7:14 — humbling → prayer → seeking God's face → turning from wickedness: humbling is the first and foundational act of the person's movement toward God, preceding and enabling the further movements of prayer and seeking. 2Ch33:12 — Manasseh "entreated the favor of the Lord his God and humbled himself greatly": the supplication is integrated with and enabled by the humbling. Jam4:10 — "humble yourselves before the Lord and he will exalt you": the directional address ("before the Lord") makes the Godward orientation of the act explicit. 1Pe5:6 — "humble yourselves under the mighty hand of God": the act is constitutively Godward. The characteristic is one of the primary forms of the human person's movement toward God.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, extensively. The gospel-obedience cluster (M09-D-VCG-01) is almost entirely Godward: Rom1:5 — obedience of faith "for the sake of his name" — submission directed toward God's honour; Rom16:26 — the will's trustful submission as "the culminating response to revealed mystery"; Heb5:9 — obedience as the ongoing inner orientation that connects the believer to salvation from Christ. 1Pe1:2 — obedience to Jesus Christ as the goal of the Spirit's sanctifying work — the Godward orientation of submission is the telos of sanctification itself. The human-to-God direction is the dominant register of the characteristic's operation.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The characteristic is constitutively Godward — both verses frame the contrite person's state as one before God (Psa34:18 — God responds to them; Isa57:15 — God dwells with them). The contrite inner state is thus implicitly a Godward orientation: the person in genuine contrition is not turned away from God but broken before him, which constitutes a movement toward God in the most acute form. The lowly posture paired with contrition in Isa57:15 ("contrite and lowly spirit") confirms the Godward direction — the characteristic includes within it the lowly orientation that opens toward God.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence meekness or gentleness operating in the human person's movement toward God (seeking, prayer, worship). Heb5:2 addresses the high priest's movement toward the erring on God's behalf; Act9:38 addresses Peter's movement toward those in need. The Godward direction of the characteristic is not directly evidenced in §3.C.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

1Ti2:2 — "godly and dignified in every way" — the dignified manner of life is paired with godliness (eusebeia — God-directed life). The semnotēs is thus the characteristic that shapes how the person inhabits their God-directed life in the public sphere. The characteristic operates in the human-toward-God movement by providing the manner-quality with which the person inhabits their godly life — not as a movement toward God specifically but as the quality of how they live before God and others.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Yes — the characteristic is constitutively a human-toward-God movement. All five verses evidence this direction: Exo35:5 — "contribution to the Lord" (toward God); Exo35:22 — gold brought to God's tabernacle; 1Ch28:21 — service for the house of God; 2Ch29:31 — burnt offerings and thank offerings (toward God); Psa51:12 — joyfully, freely-offered devotion (toward God). The freely-moved heart's movement is consistently Godward — willing-heartedness is the human movement toward God in its most genuine and uncoerced form.

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The inner posture required for genuine Godward humbling is evidenced across multiple verses. *Heart-tenderness:* 2Ch34:27 — "your heart was tender" — genuine receptivity of the inner person to being addressed and moved. *Genuine acknowledgment of God's rightness:* 2Ch12:6 — "the Lord is righteous" — the cognitive-moral act of affirming God's authority and one's own inadequacy. *Recognition of one's actual situation:* 2Ki22:19 — hearing God's words as personally claiming — the inner capacity to receive divine address as genuinely relevant to oneself. *Freedom from self-enclosure:* the contrast with 2Ch36:12 (refusal to humble before the prophet) identifies the blocking condition — self-closure against divine address — and its absence as the required posture.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The inner posture required is evidenced across the M09-C corpus. *Faith-trust:* Heb11:8 — Abraham "obeyed by faith" — the trust-orientation that submits to God's word before comprehending its outcome. *Fear of God:* Phili2:12; Col3:22 — reverential awareness of God's authority rather than social-pressure compliance. *Sincere heart:* Eph6:5; Col3:22 — undivided inner genuineness rather than divided performance. *Self-denial of merit:* Luk17:10 — "we are unworthy servants; we have only done what was our duty" — the inner posture that does not claim credit for submission, precisely the posture required for the characteristic's genuineness before God.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The inner posture is the contrite and lowly spirit itself (Isa57:15). The characteristic does not require any additional posture beyond itself — genuine contrition is already the posture before God that draws his dwelling presence. The broken heart and crushed spirit (Psa34:18) constitute the Godward posture: they are an opening toward God created by the collapse of proud self-sufficiency that normally stands between the person and genuine divine encounter.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on the inner posture required for the characteristic's Godward operation. The characteristic in this corpus operates primarily in the human-toward-others direction rather than the human-toward-God direction.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The inner posture required for semnotēs is established across all three verses: genuine inner character gravity (not performed), paired with godliness (1Ti2:2) and integrity (Tit2:7). The posture required is settled authentic inner-grounded seriousness rather than anxious external performance of gravity. This requires genuine inner formation rather than surface-level manner adoption.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The inner posture required for the human-toward-God movement evidenced by this characteristic is the *freely-moved, uncoerced inner orientation toward God*. Exo35:5 — "whoever is of a willing heart" — the posture is the heart genuinely moving from within rather than under external compulsion. Psa51:12 — the willing spirit as divine gift needed to sustain the movement toward God — implies that genuine posture requires divine upholding when the person's own orientation has been disrupted.

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The human-toward-God direction reveals that genuine relationship with God is constitutively asymmetrical: the creature before the Creator is in a posture of dependence and acknowledging that dependence is the characteristic's inner form. Mic6:8 — "walk humbly with your God" — names this as a comprehensive orientation of the whole life: the person's walk with God is structured by the posture of humility, not equality. The exaltation-pattern (1Pe5:6; Mat23:12) reveals that genuine relationship with God involves the person taking the lower place and receiving the reversal as God's gift rather than claiming it as their right. The relationship is one in which God's sovereignty and human creatureliness are genuine, acknowledged, and the foundation of the connexion rather than obstacles to it.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that the person's relationship with God is constitutively authority-structured: the person who genuinely submits is one who has accepted that God's authority is real, legitimate, and the organizing principle of their inner life (Rom6:16/17 — whose authority determines the will's orientation). The relationship is not one of equals but of creature genuinely receiving and responding to the Creator's authority — which is, paradoxically, not diminishing but liberating (Rom6:17 — transformation from sin's slavery to righteousness through heart-obedience). The direction also reveals that the relationship is relational-responsive rather than self-generated: the person's movement toward God is a response to God's prior address.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that genuine relationship with God requires the person's genuine inner reality rather than a managed or constructed presentation. Isa57:15 — the high-and-holy God dwelling with the contrite — implies that what attracts God's dwelling presence is not religious performance or outward achievement but the person's genuine inner moral reality, honestly held. The relationship is one in which the person's authentic brokenness before God is the ground of the deepest divine-human encounter.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on the human-to-God direction for this characteristic. Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

1Ti2:2's pairing of dignified with godly reveals that the person's relationship with God is reflected in how they inhabit their whole manner of life — the dignity is the outward character-quality of life genuinely lived before God. The relationship with God produces and requires the characteristic as its social expression: godliness (inner orientation toward God) manifests in dignity (the quality of manner in which God-directed life is inhabited in the world).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The Godward direction of willing-heartedness reveals that the person's relationship with God is at its most genuine when the movement toward him is freely-given rather than compelled. Exo35:5/22's free-will offering and 2Ch29:31's beyond-required worship evidence a relationship in which the person moves toward God from genuine inner desire rather than external obligation — this is the relational quality that willing-heartedness contributes: genuine freely-given rather than duty-produced relation.

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the human-toward-God direction is extensively evidenced (see T4.2.1–T4.2.3).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; human-to-God operation is extensively evidenced (see T4.2.1–T4.2.3).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the Godward orientation of the characteristic is constitutive of its identity (see T4.2.1–T4.2.3).

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The evidence is silent on the human-to-God direction of this characteristic in §3.C. The characteristic in this corpus operates in the God-mediated-toward-human (Heb5:2) and human-toward-human-in-need (Act9:38) directions.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The human-to-God dimension is evidenced through the godliness-pairing in 1Ti2:2 (see T4.2.1–T4.2.3).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the Godward direction is the dominant relational direction of this characteristic (see T4.2.1–T4.2.3).

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, in the horizontal dimension. Phili2:3 — "in humility count others more significant than yourselves" — is the definitive statement of humility as given from one person toward another: the cognitive-volitional reordering that elevates others in the person's own estimation. Eph4:2 — "with all humility and gentleness… bearing with one another in love" — positions humility as the disposition that enables genuine bearing with others in their differences and failings. 1Pe5:5 — "clothe yourselves with humility toward one another" — the relational direction is explicit ("toward one another"). 2Cor11:7 — Paul humbling himself by taking an unpaid role "so that you might be exalted" — the self-lowering explicitly serves the other's elevation. The characteristic in its human-horizontal form is constitutively other-directed: the humble person takes the lower place so the other can receive the higher.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, in the household and apostolic registers. The household obedience patterns (M09-D-VCG-03 — Eph6:1; Col3:20; 1Ti3:4; Pro30:17) all involve a person extending submission toward another in a legitimate authority structure. 1Ti3:4 — children's submissiveness in the overseer's household — evidences submission as extended by children toward parental authority. 1Ti2:11 — the woman's submissiveness in learning — is submission extended toward the teaching authority. The apostolic register (Phili2:12; 2Th3:14; Phile21) evidences submission extended toward apostolic authority. In the giving direction, Paul "gives" or "receives" the community's submission (2Cor7:15 — Titus receiving the Corinthians' obedient welcome).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence contrition being extended horizontally by one person toward another. The characteristic in this corpus is exclusively Godward in its relational direction — the contrite person before God, and God's response to the contrite person. The horizontal dimension of contrition (e.g., contrition toward another person one has wronged) is not evidenced in §3.B.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Yes — Act9:38 evidences the horizontal extension most directly: Peter is expected to exercise the unimpeded responsiveness (okneō absence) of going to Tabitha's community in their need — the disciples expect Peter to come immediately, without self-protective hesitation. The extension is: Peter toward the community in Joppa who have called for help. Heb5:2 evidences the priestly-mediating extension: the high priest extends metriopatheō toward the ignorant and wayward — one person (the high priest) dealing gently with others (the erring people). Both verses evidence horizontal extension of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes, in the leadership and teaching contexts. 1Ti3:4 — the overseer extends dignity toward his children through the manner of his household governance — his semnotēs is something that reaches the children and produces ordered compliance. Tit2:7 — the teacher extends dignity toward his hearers through the manner of teaching — the semnotēs is something that reaches the learners and authenticates the instruction. Both evidence horizontal extension: leader/teacher toward those in their charge.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

1Ch28:21 — "every willing man who has skill for any kind of service; also the officers and all the people will be wholly at your command" — the willing craftsmen extend their willing-hearted skilled service toward Solomon and the corporate project. The horizontal extension is the willing person placing their service fully at the disposal of the community's leadership and corporate purpose. The free-giving of skilled service to the temple-building project is willing-heartedness extended horizontally within the community.

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The conditions for genuine horizontal extension follow from the M09-A voluntary register. First, *genuine other-regard*: Phili2:3 requires the cognitive reordering of counting others more significant — the giver must genuinely arrive at an other-centred evaluation, not a performed one. Second, *freedom from conceit and selfish ambition*: Phili2:3 frames humility as the direct counter to "selfish ambition and conceit" — the giver must be free from the self-asserting drives that reverse the other-direction. Third, *the character-disposition*: Col3:12 — humility as a character-garment — suggests the giver must have the settled inner disposition, not merely the momentary act; Eph4:2 names it as "all humility" — the whole, not partial, disposition. Fourth, *the Christological pattern* (Phili2:5–8) suggests that genuine horizontal extension requires the same volitional self-giving that characterises Christ's own humbling.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The enabling inner conditions in the giver (the one who submits) are: *Theological motivation:* Eph6:1 ("in the Lord, for this is right") and Col3:20 ("for this pleases the Lord") — the submission is enabled by the theologically grounded conviction that the authority is legitimate and the submission is right. *Sincere-heart genuineness:* Eph6:5; Col3:22 — undivided inner motive rather than divided performance. *Fear of God as deepest motivator:* Phili2:12 ("fear and trembling"); Col3:22 ("fearing the Lord") — the reverential affect that sustains submission beyond social pressure. *Self-assessment of unworthiness:* Luk17:10 — the inner posture of not claiming merit for having submitted — enabling the characteristic's genuine form without pride in submission.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on horizontal extension of contrition (see T4.3.1). Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 directly evidences the enabling condition: genuine awareness of one's own shared creaturely weakness ("he himself is beset with weakness"). The giver of metriopatheō can only extend genuine gentleness from a ground of honest self-knowledge about their own limitation. Additionally, the Act9:38 context implies that the inner condition of genuine readiness (absence of self-protective hesitation) is what enables the extension of prompt responsiveness — the giver must have no internal friction that delays their response to genuine need.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Genuine inner formation rather than performed manner is the enabling condition: Tit2:7's pairing with integrity confirms that the dignity must be genuine (backed by moral integrity) rather than performed (mere gravity without inner-grounded worth). The person who extends genuine semnotēs must have it as a real character quality, not as a social performance — the difference between the two is evidenced by whether the characteristic produces ordered response (1Ti3:4 — genuine semnotēs produces compliance) or merely performance-that-the-children-see-through.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The enabling condition evidenced throughout the corpus is the *genuine freedom of the inner movement*: Exo35:5 — "whoever is of a willing heart" — the heart's own genuine free movement is the enabling condition. The person who gives from willing-heartedness gives because the heart is genuinely moved, not because external conditions require it. Psa51:12 adds the condition of *divine upholding* when the person's own inner freedom has been disrupted — genuine extension of the characteristic after failure requires divine restoration.

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The Phili2 passage provides the clearest answer: the human call to humility (v.3 — "count others more significant") is grounded in Christ's prior self-humbling (v.8) and in the Trinitarian life of self-giving that the Incarnation expresses. This suggests the giver must have *received* the pattern and spirit of Christ's self-lowering before they can genuinely give it — the characteristic flows from an inner alignment with the kenotic movement of the Son. Col3:12 ("put on… humility, as God's chosen ones, holy and beloved") links the capacity for the character-disposition to the status of being known and loved by God — the person who has received divine acceptance does not need to assert themselves, and from that security can genuinely lower themselves for others. The security of being received by God enables the person to give the posture of lowering toward others.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The corpus evidences two foundational prerequisites. First, *reception of the gospel and obedience of faith:* 2Cor9:13 — submission "flows directly from confession of the gospel" — the person must have genuinely received the gospel and made the primary submission of faith before they can genuinely extend submission in other relationships. The primary Godward submission is the enabling condition for horizontal submission. Second, *formation through experience:* Heb5:8 — Christ's learning of obedience through suffering — the capacity for genuine submission in hard circumstances requires prior formation through costly engagement. Phili2:12's sustained obedience implies a sustained formation that precedes the sustained expression.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on the horizontal giving direction (see T4.3.1). Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 provides the answer: the high priest must have genuinely experienced and accepted his own creaturely weakness before he can extend genuine gentleness toward the erring. The characteristic requires having genuinely reckoned with one's own limitation rather than suppressed or denied it. The person who can give metriopatheō is one who has received (or accepted) their own creaturely condition honestly — not transcended it, but genuinely inhabited it without self-deception.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The person must have genuinely formed the inner character quality — 1Ti3:4's "with all dignity" and Tit2:7's "show integrity, dignity" are standards for persons who have already formed the characteristic rather than descriptions of its acquisition. The person giving semnotēs must have genuinely inhabited the character gravity through formation in godliness (1Ti2:2 — pairing) and moral integrity (Tit2:7 — pairing) before it can be genuinely extended.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

In VCG-01, the person must have a genuinely free inner orientation toward God — the willing heart is a given of their inner life rather than something requiring prior reception. In VCG-02 (Psa51:12), the person must have received the divine restoration of the willing spirit through God's upholding — after failure, the restoration precedes the renewed expression. The most profound answer the corpus gives: the person must have received (or had restored) the divine gift of the willing spirit (Psa51:12) before they can genuinely give from that spirit rather than from compelled compliance.

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the giving direction is evidenced (see T4.3.1–T4.3.3).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the giving direction is evidenced (see T4.3.1–T4.3.3).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on the horizontal giving direction. The characteristic in this corpus operates exclusively in the vertical (human-to-God and God-to-human) dimension.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (see T4.3.1–T4.3.3).

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (see T4.3.1–T4.3.3).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (see T4.3.1–T4.3.3).

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The receiving direction is less directly evidenced than the giving direction, but it is present. In Luk1:48, Mary receives the divine acknowledgement of her humble estate — God looks upon her humility and she receives his favour as a consequence. In the horizontal direction, the community that encounters Paul's humility (Act20:19; 2Cor11:7) receives the benefit of his self-lowering — the Corinthians' exaltation (2Cor11:7) is the received effect of Paul's self-humbling. In Eph4:2 and Phili2:3, the posture of humility toward one another creates a relational environment that the other person receives as genuine regard. The receiving of humility from another is evidenced as the reception of the other's genuine regard and self-lowering on one's behalf.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

Yes, in the community and apostolic registers. 2Cor7:15 — Titus receives the Corinthians' obedient welcome with fear and trembling; his affection deepens in response. Phile21 — Paul writes with confidence that Philemon's obedience will be received (he will receive the expression of Philemon's submission). 1Ti3:4 — the overseer whose children are submissive receives their submission as a sign of his household order and character. The person in authority receives the submission as both a relational expression and a vindication of the authority structure.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence contrition being received horizontally from another person. The characteristic is a state the person is in before God; its reception in the sense of one person receiving contrition from another is not evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 evidences reception: the "ignorant and wayward" receive the high priest's metriopatheō — they are the recipients of his measured gentle dealing. The erring persons receive a form of engagement that is calibrated and compassionate rather than severe. The receiving of this characteristic is the experience of being dealt with gently rather than harshly when one has erred.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

Yes. 1Ti3:4 — the overseer's children receive the effects of his semnotēs in the form of orderly, respectful compliance — they receive the character-quality's relational ordering. Tit2:7 — the hearers receive teaching that is authenticated by the teacher's semnotēs — they receive instruction whose credibility is established by the teacher's dignity. The reception is not the characteristic itself but its effects: orderly response and authentic teaching-reception.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

1Ch28:21 — Solomon and the temple-building project receive the willing-hearted service of the craftsmen — their service is received as a gift of willing engagement rather than compelled labour. God receives the willing-hearted offerings (Exo35:5/22; 2Ch29:31) — the willing-hearted person extends free offering; God receives it. The receiving direction is most clearly evidenced in God's reception of the free offerings and in Solomon's reception of the willing skilled service.

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The corpus does not directly address the inner conditions that enable or block a person's reception of another's humility toward them. The evidence focuses on the giver's conditions (T4.3.2) and the Godward reception (T4.2). This is an evidence gap for the horizontal receiving direction — the corpus does not specify what inner conditions in the recipient enable genuine reception of another's humble regard.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The corpus addresses the receiver's inner conditions primarily through the authority-figure lens. The authority who receives submission must genuinely hold legitimate authority (Gal2:5 — false teachers do not receive Paul's submission; their illegitimacy disqualifies them). The authority's character shapes the quality of submission received: 1Ti3:4 — the overseer's household order reflects his character, and his children's submission is received as an evidence of his fitness for leadership. The corpus does not address the inner conditions of a non-authority person receiving submission from another.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

Evidence is silent on horizontal reception of this characteristic (see T4.4.1). Prompt closed.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly address the inner conditions of the recipient that enable or block reception of another's meekness/gentleness. The focus is on the giver's enabling conditions (Heb5:2 — shared weakness) rather than the receiver's conditions.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not directly address the inner conditions of the recipients (children, learners) that enable or block their reception of the leader's or teacher's semnotēs. The evidence focuses on the characteristics of the giver rather than the receiver's inner conditions.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The corpus does not directly address the inner conditions of those who receive another's willing-hearted giving (what enables or blocks their reception). The evidence focuses on the inner conditions of the giver rather than the receiver.

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The corpus does not directly address what happens in the person who encounters another's humility but does not receive it. The evidence focuses on pride as the internal state that cannot receive God's grace (Jam4:6 — God opposes the proud) but does not specify the inner state of one who encounters human humility and rejects it. This remains an evidence gap in the horizontal receiving dimension.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

In the gospel-obedience register, 2Th1:8 names the inner state of the non-receiver: "those who do not obey the gospel" face divine judgment and are in a state of "not knowing God." The inner refusal to receive the submission-claim of the gospel is a state of fundamental relational rupture. 2Th3:14 — the non-receiver of apostolic instruction is to be "shamed" by communal response — the assumption is that the non-receiver is in a state of inner refusal that shame might awaken to repentance. The inner state is thus one of active refusal rather than mere ignorance: the person encounters the authority's claim and refuses the yielding it requires.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence addresses this only in the vertical direction: the person who does not receive the possibility of genuine contrition (i.e., remains hardened or self-justifying before God) is implied as the structural opposite in Isa57:15's contrast — but this is not directly addressed in the two-verse corpus as a named inner state.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The corpus does not directly address the inner state of one who encounters another's gentleness and does not receive it. The evidence addresses the giver's conditions, not the non-receiving recipient's inner state.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The corpus does not directly address the inner state of those who encounter semnotēs but do not receive its ordering effects. The evidence addresses the giver's character without describing those who are unresponsive to it.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The corpus does not directly address the inner state of persons who encounter another's willing-heartedness but do not receive it (e.g., leadership that dismisses willing service). The evidence describes the givers and recipients who are present and receiving rather than those who reject.

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is partially silent on the horizontal receiving dimension specifically (see T4.4.2 and T4.4.3). The receiving of God's grace and mercy in response to one's humbling is extensively evidenced (divine direction — T4.1); the reception of another person's humility toward oneself is less directly evidenced. This gap is noted.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence addresses the receiving direction, primarily in the authority-figure and gospel-non-compliance registers (see T4.4.1–T4.4.3). The person-receiving-another's-submission register is less extensively developed, though evidenced in 2Cor7:15 and Phile21.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The evidence is silent on horizontal receiving of the characteristic. The characteristic's operation in this corpus is Godward and divinely-responsive, not horizontal.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The receiving direction is partially evidenced (Heb5:2 — the erring receive metriopatheō). The inner conditions of reception and the state of the non-receiver are not addressed in §3.C (see T4.4.2 and T4.4.3).

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The receiving direction is partially evidenced (the effects received — orderly compliance, authenticated teaching reception). The inner conditions of reception and the state of the non-receiver are not addressed (see T4.4.2 and T4.4.3).

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The receiving direction is partially evidenced (God and Solomon as recipients — T4.4.1). The inner conditions of reception and the state of the non-receiver are not directly addressed (T4.4.2 and T4.4.3 — silent).

---

#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence shows operation in both contexts without explicit contrast between them. The ka.na corpus operates primarily within the covenantal bond (Israel before God, Israelite kings before the covenant Lord); the horizontal humility in Phili2:3 and Eph4:2 operates within the body of believers. However, 2Ch30:11 evidences humility crossing tribal and political divisions — "men of Asher, of Manasseh, and of Zebulun" overcoming their northern-kingdom separation from Jerusalem through the inner act of humbling. This suggests the characteristic can operate across relational distance and social division. Mat11:29 — the invitation to learn humility from Jesus — crosses the distance between the divine teacher and all who are "weary and burdened," suggesting the characteristic operates beyond existing relational bonds.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The household register (Eph6:1; Col3:20; Pro30:17; 1Ti3:4) evidences the characteristic operating within the closest existing bonds (family). The gospel-obedience register (Act6:7; Rom1:5; 16:26) evidences it operating across the broadest possible scope (all nations). The characteristic operates in both — within close bonds and across distance — but the inner quality varies: within close bonds, the household submission is shaped by long-term formation (1Ti3:4 — cultivated household quality); across the broader gospel scope, the submission is the decisive single act of reorientation (Act6:7 — priests becoming obedient to the faith). The characteristic adapts its operational form to the relational context.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly address relational-bond variation. Both verses operate in the divine-human relational register without specifying whether the human is within covenant or outside it. Psa34:18 uses generalising language ("the brokenhearted," "the crushed in spirit") without covenant-specificity; Isa57:15 similarly uses the general "him who is of a contrite and lowly spirit."

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 operates within the established priestly covenant structure — the metriopatheō is the high priest's characteristic within his covenantally-defined mediating role. Act9:38 operates within the early Christian community network (disciples in Joppa calling for Peter in Lydda) — the responsive readiness is called for within the network of believers. Both evidences operate within established relational structures rather than across relational distance; the characteristic appears to be expressed within existing relational frameworks where the person has a defined role or relationship.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The three verses evidence the characteristic operating within established relational structures: the civic community (1Ti2:2 — under governance), the household (1Ti3:4 — within the family), and the teaching relationship (Tit2:7 — between teacher and learners). All three are existing relational bonds rather than across relational distance. The characteristic appears particularly suited to ordering established authority-relationships rather than crossing relational distance.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating primarily within established covenantal and communal structures: the Israel community at Sinai (Exo35 — within the covenant people), the pre-temple Israel community (1Ch28:21), the temple-restoration community under Hezekiah (2Ch29:31), and the individual psalmist's relationship with God (Psa51:12). The characteristic operates within existing relational structures rather than across relational distance.

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The primary evidence is covenantal (Israel before God; believers in the body). However, the exaltation-of-the-humble pattern (Luk1:52 — "he has exalted those of humble estate") and the wisdom connexion (Pro11:2 — structural contrast available to any person) operate as wisdom-principles that appear cross-covenantal in their scope. The characteristic's operation is most extensively evidenced in the covenantal context, but its wisdom-principle dimension suggests it operates beyond those boundaries.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. Gen49:10 — "the obedience of the peoples" (all nations) — the submission characteristic is framed as gathering all peoples, not only Israel. Rom1:5 — "obedience of faith for the sake of his name among all the nations" — the scope is universal. Pro30:17 — obedience to parents as a creational-wisdom principle, not specifically covenantal. The characteristic operates within covenant but also extends to universal scope in its eschatological and wisdom dimensions.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The generalising language of both verses (Psa34:18 — general wisdom-type statement; Isa57:15 — general address) suggests the characteristic may operate across covenantal contexts rather than being restricted to the covenant people. The God who is near to "the brokenhearted" is not specifying Israelites only. However, both verses arise within the OT canonical context which has Israel as its primary frame, so a definitive cross-covenantal claim requires caution from this corpus alone.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 operates within the covenantal-priestly structure. Act9:38 operates within the early Christian community. The evidence is covenantal in frame. However, the generalising quality of metriopatheō (measured-compassionate restraint toward the erring) as an inner capacity suggests it may operate beyond specifically covenantal contexts wherever the person encounters the ignorant and wayward — the capacity is not inherently limited to covenant insiders.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

1Ti2:2 — "a peaceful and quiet life under good governance" in public civic life — the characteristic is called for in the public civic sphere which is not narrowly covenantal. The characteristic thus crosses the covenantal boundary into the broader civic sphere, where the believer's semnotēs shapes their manner of inhabiting public life. Tit2:7's teaching context and 1Ti3:4's household context are community-formational, while 1Ti2:2's civic context is broader.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The five-verse corpus is exclusively within covenantal contexts: the Israel covenant community (Exo35; 1Ch28:21; 2Ch29:31) and the individual covenant-member's relation to God (Psa51:12). The characteristic as evidenced in §3.E operates within the covenant rather than across covenantal boundaries. The generalising principle of free-will offering may extend beyond the covenantal context, but the direct evidence is covenantal.

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The characteristic's relational scope is extensive. Vertically: the humble before God includes all who take the posture (2Ch7:14 — "my people who are called by my name"; Jam4:6 — "to the humble" without restriction within the community). Horizontally: Phili2:3 and Eph4:2 address believers toward one another; Col3:12 extends to "God's chosen ones." The evidence does not restrict the horizontal scope to any particular subgroup within the community — "one another" is the inclusive relational scope. There is no verse evidencing humility as appropriately withheld from any person.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The scope is broad. The gospel-obedience register (Rom1:5; 16:26; Act6:7) includes all who receive the gospel without restriction. The household register (Eph6:1; Col3:20; Pro30:17) includes all within family structures. The eschatological register (Gen49:10 — all peoples; Heb5:9 — all who obey him) has universal scope. The Gal2:5 instance (submission withheld from false teachers) establishes the one exclusion: submission to illegitimate authority that would compromise truth is explicitly excluded. The scope is thus: all who encounter legitimate authority; none who would be required to submit to what is illegitimate or gospel-distorting.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

Both verses use inclusive, non-restrictive language: "the brokenhearted," "the crushed in spirit" (Psa34:18) — any person in that inner state; "him who is of a contrite and lowly spirit" (Isa57:15) — any person of that character. The relational scope appears to be constituted by the inner state itself rather than by external markers (covenant membership, ethnicity, status). God's nearness and dwelling are responsive to the inner condition, not to external identity markers.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

Heb5:2 — the "ignorant and wayward" (agnooumenois kai planōmenois) — describes the scope as those who err through ignorance or waywardness, without specifying covenant membership. The relational scope of metriopatheō appears to be constituted by the erring person's condition rather than their covenantal status. Act9:38's scope is the community in need. Together: the characteristic's scope extends to anyone in the condition (wayward, in need) that occasions the response.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The relational scope of semnotēs spans the civic, household, and pedagogical spheres — broad rather than narrow. The characteristic is required "in every way" (1Ti2:2) — the comprehensive scope implies it should characterise the believer's presence in all relational contexts rather than being confined to specific situations.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

Exo35:5 — "whoever is of a willing heart" — within the covenant community, the scope includes all whose hearts are genuinely willing regardless of gender (Exo35:22 — "both men and women") or specific role (1Ch28:21 — craftsmen of all skills). Within the covenantal community, willing-heartedness is inclusive of all who genuinely have the inner disposition rather than confined to a priestly or leadership class.

---

##### T4.5.4 — If the evidence is silent on relational boundaries, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is not silent but is less precise on scope boundaries than on the characteristic's core operation (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3).

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The evidence is not silent; relational scope and boundary are evidenced (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3).

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (E)

The evidence is not silent but is limited in precision (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3). The scope appears inclusive and the primary qualifier is the inner state rather than external identity.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (E)

The evidence addresses relational scope partially (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3). The corpus evidences covenantal-structural contexts without definitively excluding cross-covenantal scope.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (E)

The evidence addresses relational scope (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3). The scope is broad (civic, household, pedagogical) with the comprehensive "in every way" implying no relational exclusion.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (E)

The evidence addresses relational scope (see T4.5.1–T4.5.3). The scope is within the covenant community, inclusive of all genuinely willing-hearted members regardless of gender or role.

---

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The Humility corpus does not directly evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The characteristic's relational structure in the evidence is God-ward and human-ward.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The Submission corpus does not directly evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The characteristic's relational structure in the evidence is constitutively human-to-divine and human-to-human.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not directly evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The relational structure in both verses is exclusively divine-human.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The two-verse corpus does not evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The three-verse corpus does not evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The five-verse corpus does not evidence the characteristic operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings.

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

Yes, through the distortion that the Colossian material evidences. Col2:18 — insisting on "asceticism and worship of angels, going on in detail about visions, puffed up without reason by his sensuous mind" — the false humility condemned here involves *worship of angels* alongside the self-referential asceticism. This suggests adversarial distortion is operating: a counterfeit humility that is in fact pride-driven and involves spiritual activity (angel-worship, visions) that the apostle identifies as corrupted inner life. The characteristic is distorted rather than straightforwardly attacked, but Col2:18 evidences that the site of humility can be occupied by a counterfeit that serves pride and false spirituality.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (E)

The corpus implies adversarial dimension through 2Cor10:5 — "arguments and every lofty opinion raised against the knowledge of God" — the cognitive resistance to submission is framed as something that must be actively "destroyed"; the proud reasoning that resists Christ's authority operates as a structural adversarial force within the inner person. Whether this implies a spiritual adversarial source is not directly stated in this corpus, but the battle-language of 2Cor10:5 (destroying strongholds, taking thoughts captive) implies a warfare dimension. The characteristic is the ground being contended for in this cognitive-spiritual battle.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The corpus does not directly evidence adversarial activity targeting contrition. The structural opposite (hardening, self-justification, unrepentance) is not framed in this corpus as adversarial attack; it is more directly the person's own self-protective response.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The corpus does not directly evidence adversarial activity targeting meekness or gentleness. The structural opposites (severity, hesitation) are not framed as adversarial attack in this corpus.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The corpus does not directly evidence adversarial activity targeting semnotēs. The structural opposite (M08 — proud self-display) is not framed as adversarial attack in this corpus.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The corpus does not directly evidence adversarial activity targeting willing-heartedness. Psa51:12's loss of the willing spirit is attributed to moral failure rather than adversarial attack.

---

##### T4.6.3 — Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation or strengthening of the humility characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Submission** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation or strengthening of the submission characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Contrition** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Meekness and gentleness** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Dignity** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Willing-heartedness** (S)

The corpus does not evidence angelic mediation of willing-heartedness.

---

##### T4.6.4 — If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Humility** (E)

The evidence is largely silent except for the adversarial-distortion dimension evidenced in Col2:18 (see T4.6.2). Angelic communication or mediation of the characteristic is not evidenced.
